Espingarda Mauser Modelo 1908
Mauser M08
The Mauser Model 1908 was an exceptionally long rifle based on the Mauser 1898 and chambered in 7x57mm Mauser. It was originally produced for Brazil by the German company DWM, but Brazil has subsequently begun to produce staggering quantities of the rifle domestically, and it became a staple in many state armies as time went it became almost synonym with the Interstate War in the cultural mindset of the nation. The Piratini state's army used the same gear as the other states that formed Brazil, and alongside the southern states it was the premier fighting force of the region.
Fusil Mauser Modelo 1935
Mauser M35
The Mauser Rifle Model 1935 is a unique Mauser Rifle which utilises a 7x57mm cartridge produced domestically by Brazil and abroad in close conjunction with the Mauser company, as part of the extensive collaboration between the Brazilian and German governments. Said collaboration started in the 1910s, as a clique officers then derided as 'the Young Turks' by the press began lobbying extensively for closer cooperation with the global hegemon. Everything from helmets to artillery pieces started to be fashioned after the German model, and as such a modernisation of the older Mausers became a priority. This firearm became almost synonymous with the Brazilian military during the Weltkrieg.
Submetralhadora Bergmann Modelo 1938
Bergmann M38
During the late years of the Pessoa presidency, Brazil purchased a relatively small number of Bergmann MP28 submachine guns, but they never saw much use outside of national guard regiments in Rio itself; The M38 is a simplified and easily manufactured derivative of the MP28 created in response to growing tensions in South America, and was intended to be the standard issue firearm for the entire Brazilian military and was produced in large quantities in foundries across the country and as such became almost synonymous with the Brazilian military during the Weltkrieg period.
Mosquetão Semi-Automático Rossi Modelo 1944
As the Second Weltkrieg raged in Europe, Brazilian leadership found that their weapons were simply outmatched as the arms race between the great powers, and rather than try to catch up, it simply started producing an outright copy of the newest German semi automatic rifle designs such as the G41. The first models were made in the Rossi foundry in Rio Grande do Sul, wherein the model takes its name from. While more advanced than other weapons in use by the Paulista army, its low reliability made it unpopular with soldiers, who often preferred older models or even captured gear.
Rossi M44
Metralhadora M.08/15 & Morteiro de 7,58-cm
The Weltkrieg saw the introduction of some of the deadliest weapons known to man, such as the fearsome M.G. Modell 08/15. In the close confines of trench warfare, the once archaic mortar was brought back to relevance. Many of these older piece of equipment were among the hardware directly sold or leased to Brazil over the course of the military mission from Germany in that nation.
Metralhadora M34 & Morteiro de 8cm
The Machine Gun Model 34 (MG34) was a recoil operated air-cooled machine gun. Chambered in the powerful 7.92x57-mm Mauser rifle cartridge, the machine gun's high rate of fire (900 RPM) and efficient mobility made it arguably the most advanced machine gun in the world at the time; and was eagerly shown to Brazil as a proof of the martial superiority of the Kaiserreich. The perhaps unexpected consequence of that was the fact that the design was copied with little regard for patents by the Rio government after Black Monday. The Mortar Model 34 is an infantry mortar that employs 8-cm shells. It has been noted for its high accuracy and rate of fire.
Metralhadora M39 & Morteiro 'Torneira' de 20cm
The Machine Gun Model 39 (M.G. 39) was an improvement over the M.G. 34. This belt fed machine gun features a high rate of fire and is suited for all purposes. The 20-cm leichter Mortar Model 40 is a spigot mortar designed for striking obstacles and strong points. Brazilian copies were noted for having inferior quality materials in their fabrication, presumably to lower costs.
Metralhadora Imbel M1 & Morteiro de 8cm
The first models of heavy machine guns produced by Brazil, for Brazil, the Imbel models were noted for very high rate of fire, but also relatively low reliability and durability due to several corners cut during production. When it was working properly, it was one of the most fearsome weapons in the country's arsenal, however.
Metralhadora Anti-Tanque Imbel .50
The first models of heavy machine guns produced by Brazil, for Brazil, the Imbel models were noted for very high rate of fire, but also relatively low reliability and durability due to several corners cut during production. When it was working properly, it was one of the most fearsome weapons in the country's arsenal, however. Heavier variants were assigned to Anti Tank duties in the lack of proper weapons for the task in the armed forces.
Lança Rojão M44
The Model 44 Rocket Launcher, like many Brazilian weapons of its time, is a rather uninspired copy of European equipment used in the Second Weltkrieg, later produced and used by Brazil itself. Based mostly on the German 'Panzerschreck', the weapon shares most specifications with it, including its 8,8-centimetre rockets and the massive smoke trail left by firing.
Obuseiro Rheinmetall de 10,5 cm
After a series of military missions from and to Germany, Brazil's government started to import foreign artillery from that nation. These were Rheinmetall models were relatively modern for their time, but the nation had a very limited capacity for mass production of these at home. These guns were a significant upgrade from previous models used by Germany especially when it comes to hitting moving targets.
Obuseiro Modelo 41 de 11,5cm
The Obuseiro Modelo 41 was little more than a copy of the specifications of the Modell 36 field howitzer from the German army, but with some tweaks to lower production costs, at the expense of some reliability. Even so, the gun was extensively used by artillery in Brazil across the Weltkrieg period, and was the first piece of artillery mass produced domestically itself rather than being mostly imported.
Obuseiro Modelo 43 de 17cm
Still following the trend of copying specifications from German pieces of equipment, the 1943 update of the M41 had a slight increase in firepower, and some refinements with the intent of making it more reliable. However, production was limited during wartime, and the upgraded field gun was a rare sight over the early 1940s. In later years, however, it and models with minimal variations were used by the Paulista army until the 1960s.
Ob. Rm. de 10,5 cm
Ob. M41 de 11,5cm
Ob. M43 de 17cm
CAA M2 de 2cm
CAA M5 de 3,7cm
CAA M7 de 8,8cm
Canhão Antiaéreo M2 de 2cm
Anti Air weaponry was a defensive priority for Brazil, as the war between states had shown the vulnerabilities of the federal capital against aircraft despite extensive coastal and land based defences. Developed in conjunction and with support of Germany, the M1 and M2 were admittedly little more than copies of FlaK models from the early 1930s, but that was sufficient to deal with the relatively slow aircraft deployed in South America at the time.
Canhão Antiaéreo M5 de 3,7cm
As aircraft rapidly developed, several updates and changes to the standard issue M2 were made over the years, but later models of anti aircraft weaponry entirely different specifications regarding almost everything from the main axle to the size of the cannon itself. The M5 is closely related to its German cousin, the 3,7cm Fla.K 37, but is made of lower quality materials to meet the production needs of Brazil.
Canhão Antiaéreo M7 de 8,8cm
As aircraft rapidly developed, several updates and changes to the standard issue M2 were made over the years, but later models of anti aircraft weaponry entirely different specifications regarding almost everything, and the M7 is almost entirely a departure from the original design all but in role. The M7 was the first piece of anti aircraft equipment designed domestically, but even so it retained so many similarities to similar guns in use by Germany and its allies in the Weltkrieg many experts claim it wasn't a different gun at all, but rather a domestically produced variant. The cumbersome gun saw little use in Brazilian service before the war was over.
Canhão Antitanque 'Alemão' de 3,7 cm
Initially an outright import from Germany, the gun was straight up called 'Alemão' by the troops in the barracks due to its strength and obvious foreign origin, as its makers made sure to stamp imperial eagle effigies in seemingly every model. While similar models in Europe were designed to be drawn by motorised forces, Brazil used an outdated design more suited to the many horses it had available, and the lack of appropriate road infrastructure in an eventual frontline against Argentina. Said nation was the main motivator behind Brazil's move to start fabricating the piece domestically in small numbers after 1936, as the instability in that region, and having an unpredictable regime in possession of dozens of tanks, unnerved general staff in Rio.
Canhão Antitanque M2 de 7,5 cm
Developed entirely with German models as a basis, Anti Tank Artillery Model 2, or the AT2, was developed primarily against the types of heavier armour being used by European powers as the Second Weltkrieg raged. With Germany itself less than willing to cooperate with production this time, an illegally obtained piece was the basis for production domestically, which started much too late for widespread usage within the armed forces. The few models were usually distributed to divisions expected to face the burnt of enemy assaults.
Canhão Antitanque M6 de 12,8 cm
As the Weltkrieg came to a close, the armour in enemy Tanks became almost overbearing to infantry and older models of artillery alike, and Brazil's solution was yet again to mimic European designs in a cheap fashion. This domestic version of the Pa.K 43 has all of the problems of the original guns, but with lower reliability and was made with cheaper materials. Steel shortages were the main reason for the staggeringly low number of units produced during the war.
CAT Alemão de 3,7 cm
CAT de 7,5 cm
CAT M6 de 12,8 cm
Bateria Lança Foguetes de 32cm
Rocket artillery was rarely utilised by the Brazilian military during the war period, and the few pieces manufactured were direct copies of what little German equipment of the type Brazilian officers got their hands on. Following the specifications of the original models, rockets of 32cm were used in these weapons, and a lack of said rockets is exactly why they were seldom used.
Bateria Lança Foguetes de 21cm
Rocket artillery was rarely utilised by the Brazilian military during the war period, and the few pieces manufactured were direct copies of what little German equipment of the type Brazilian officers got their hands on. Changes to the size of the rockets required for usage made later models more common, but still far from standard issue and few pieces of the LF de 21cm were used in the field when compared to even the M43.

Espingarda 6,5 mm m/1904
Mauser-Vergueiro
A bolt action rifle with a long history of service, the 6,5 mm m/1904 is more commonly known by the moniker of 'Mauser-Vergueiro', as the main design of the gun is essentially that of the Mauser 98 (with a special bolt action mechanism heavily based on the Gewehr 1888) with the 6.5×58mm Vergueiro cartridge, one developed specifically for the Portuguese variant. It became the official weapon of the Portuguese Army in 1904 and continued in that capacity until the 1940s, being widely used both at home and overseas. While it was not used by Portuguese troops in the western front, as those were armed by Entente, chiefly British, supplies, it saw extensive use in Africa from Portugal, its allies in South Africa, and was also used by Germans who occasionally captured supplies in Portuguese East Africa.
Espingarda 7.92 mm m/1904/36
Mauser-Vergueiro M36
Fundamentally little more than an updated version of the Mauser-Vergueiro to work with different sets of ammunition, it was introduced to Africa amid rising tensions between Portugal and Germany, and it became associated with Portugal's heavy handed reprisals in those areas. Its usage in Europe, while less famous, was far more widespread, but it was utterly supplanted by the FBP on later years.
Carabina C.A.P Modelo 01
C.A.P M40
A prototype carbine that saw little widespread use in Portugal's army as a whole was the country's first attempt at a standard issue, nationally produced design. As such, the nationalist Integralist junta supported the development of the C.A.P carbine intensely, but by the time it was ready for production, realities on the ground made it more worthwhile to switch to the FBP overall directly from the older Mauser-Vergueiro and variants already widely in use by the armed forces.
Pistola-Metralhadora FBP M/945
FBP M/945
The FBP submachine gun is named after the acronym for the Braço de Prata Factory, the manufacturer for the weapon, a foundry owned and controlled by the Portuguese government itself. While its development started far before its widespread use among foot troops in Portugal's army, the finished model entered production too late to replace the Mauser-Vergueiro in the war. This intent was made clear by the submachine gun having, rather unusually, bayonet sockets compatible with those of the Mauser models used by Portugal throughout the conflicts of the previous decades. The so called 'machine gun pistol' (The term in Portuguese for submachine guns in general) saw extensive use throughout many years, albeit the 1945 variant fell out of use in favour of versions with semi-automatic firing and imported models, as the scale of warfare decreased in later decades after the Second Weltkrieg.
Metralhadora Vickers & Morteiro Stokes
The water cooled Vickers MG and the Stokes trench mortar were the standard support arms of the British Empire during the Weltkrieg. During its rearmament after the conflict, the restored Portuguese monarchy purchased and fabricated them with the intention of widespread use among infantry both at home and overseas.
Metralhadora Lewis Modelo DEMS & Morteiro SBML de 2 Polegadas
With its iconic 'pan' magazine, the Lewis served the Entente since the darkest days of the First Weltkrieg. The MKIII variant had a pistol grip that allowed it to be fired from the shoulder on any part of a ship's deck. The SBML, while small, is incredibly portable and had greater firepower and range than most rifle grenades.
Metralhadora Vickers Modelo II & Morteiro ML de 3 Polegadas
The Mark II variant of the Vickers MG featured a selective fire option and a pistol grip. It had been primarily adopted for the armoured vehicles. The ML 3 inch mortar was a considerable upgrade from the Stokes, as it was reliable and sturdy for close artillery support.
Metralhadora Vickers-Vedras & Morteiro de 4.2 Polegadas
The third variant of the esteemed Vickers machine gun was designed for anti-aircraft usage and features a slightly increased rate of fire from its predecessors. Likewise, the 4.2 inch mortar was a heavier upgrade of previous Canadian mortar models and capable of dropping intense and effective support.
Morteiro-Bombarda
Developed in Canada and sold in substantial amounts to Portugal, the mortar design was that of a 'spigot' mortar. Arguing that the design could serve as both an artillery piece and an anti-tank weapon, the design was eagerly adopted by several allies of the Entente, including Portugal.
LATI
With the need for a hand-held anti tank weapon for use on the frontlines, the LATI (A direct translation of its Canadian English name) was developed based on the design of the bombard mortar. With an effective range of 105 metres in direct fire mode, the device was well liked due to its lack of backblast - however there were concerns about its intense recoil.

Ishapore SMLE Mk III
Rifle, Short, Magazine, Lee-Enfield Mk III
The Ishapore Rifle Factory was founded in 1904 and began producing the venerable Lee-Enfield (SMLE) rifle that would serve throughout the Great War. However, the loss of much of British India after the British Revolution also meant the loss of the Ishapore factory, one of the only two factories producing the SMLE outside of Britain. Many guns produced prior to the revolution still however remain in service, and more still are produced in and surrounding the former lands of the Raj.

Mauser Modelo 1909
Modelo 1909
In 1909, Peru purchased a large number of German Mauser 1898 rifles chambered in a new Spitzer variant of 7.65×53mm Mauser.
Fabrique Nationale Mauser Modelo 1935
Modelo 1935
The Fabrique Nationale Model 1935 is a slightly shortned Model 1889 Mauser with a plethora of upgrades including a new bolt and locking system, a more reliable magazine, as well as improved ergonomics. The Peruvian variant is chambered in the same Spitzer 7.65×53mm round as earlier Peruvian rifles. While Peru also purchased a number of Bohemian Model 1932 carbines, the FN-35 was much more prevalent.

Hanyang Type 88
Hanyang Type 88
Originally a product of late Guangxu era 'Self Strengthening' efforts, the Type 88 was designed as a copy of the German Gewehr 88 with export modifications. While collectively inferior to newer rifles despite improvements, and often poorly maintained, the weapon is known to be rugged and reliable if unwieldy.\n\nThis variety is mainly produced at the Hanyang Arsenal, the model's place of design, though equipment shortages often see it used alongside non-standard weapons.
Hanyang Type 27
Hanyang Type 27
Officially called the 'Type 27', this rifle was put into service in 1935 thanks to German assistance after the Qing Restoration. The weapon is functionally a near copy of the German Mauser M1924, and a considerable improvement over the much older Type 88 in terms of weight and recoil.\n\nThis variety is mainly produced at the Hanyang Arsenal with German tools, though it may not fully replace its predecessors for some time.
Tsingtao MP18
Tsingtao MP18
Thanks to the flood of Weltkrieg surplus into the world market in the early 1920s, the MP18 saw action in China some time before a modified version began production in Tsingtao.\n\nWith changes to the magazine and stock, this particular product of Sino-German cooperation has been copied and sold throughout Northern and Southern China, though primarily to the Qing Government and warlords in coastal areas.
Hanyang Type 35
Hanyang Type 35
The Type 35 is a semi-automatic rifle based on the General Liu rifle from 1914. While appearing similar, the Type 35 is shorter, has the rear of the receiver covered, and the gas-trap system replaced by a simple gas port. The new rifle is also no longer able to switch to manual action and uses magazines from the Bohemian ZH-29 rifle and ZB-26 light machine gun.

Steyr ADGZ
ADGZ
Although the Qing government and the German Empire have maintained good relations, following the outbreak of large-scale syndicalist strikes in the early 1930s, the Qing government urgently purchased a batch of Steyr ADGZs from Austria-Hungary. As the price set by the Qing government was so attractive, the Austrians even included a prototype car and blueprint. However, Germany's military assistance to the Qing government soon made these Austrian armoured vehicles obsolete.
Sonderkraftfahrzeug 231 8-rad
Haoxu 231
A symbol of Sino-German friendship, this armoured vehicle often occupied a position of prominence during Qing military parades.\n\nAccording to the opinion of the Peking-Kommission, the armoured vehicle's' eight-wheeled chassis is well suited to the characteristics of the Chinese battlefield.

Shanghai Type Zhongyuan
Zhongyuan
Following the Qing restoration, Benz AG and the Qing government established several automobile factories in China as joint ventures; the most famous being the Zhongyuan Automobile Plants located in Shanghai and Nanjing. Thousands of Type Zhongyuan trucks were produced in these two areas, which entered service in various armies loyal to the Zhili clique.\n\nNotably, the Zhongyuan is not named after the ancient Chinese place name Zhongyuan (the area surrounding the empire's core), but instead after the painted logo on the front of the truck's cab; a huge Chinese character 'Zhong' enclosed in a circle.
Sonderkraftfahrzeug 11
Haoxu 11
The Sd.Kfz. 11 (Sonderkraftfahrzeug - special motorised vehicle) was a German half-track that saw very widespread use in the Second Weltkrieg. It could carry eight troops in addition to towing a gun or trailer.
Sonderkraftfahrzeug 251
Haoxu 251
The Sd.Kfz. 251 half-track was an armoured fighting vehicle designed and first built by the Hanomag company during the Second Weltkrieg, based on their earlier Sd.Kfz. 11 vehicle.

Ross Mk III

SMLE Mk V
Carbine, Machine, Owen Mk I

SLR Mk I
Canadian National Railway Confederation U-2-a
Canadian National Railway Confederation U-2-d
Canadian National Railway Confederation U-2-e
Espingarda Mauser Modelo 1908
Mauser M08
The Mauser Model 1908 was an exceptionally long rifle based on the Mauser 1898 and chambered in 7x57mm Mauser. It was originally produced for Brazil by the German company DWM, but Brazil has subsequently begun to produce staggering quantities of the rifle domestically, and it became a staple in many state armies as time went it became almost synonym with the Interstate War in the cultural mindset of the nation. The Veracruz state's army used the same gear as the other states that formed Brazil, and alongside the southern states it was the premier fighting force of the region.
Fusil Mauser Modelo 1935
Mauser M35
The Mauser Rifle Model 1935 is a unique Mauser Rifle which utilises a 7x57mm cartridge produced domestically by Brazil and abroad in close conjunction with the Mauser company, as part of the extensive collaboration between the Brazilian and German governments. Said collaboration started in the 1910s, as a clique officers then derided as 'the Young Turks' by the press began lobbying extensively for closer cooperation with the global hegemon. Everything from helmets to artillery pieces started to be fashioned after the German model, and as such a modernisation of the older Mausers became a priority. This firearm became almost synonymous with the Brazilian military during the Weltkrieg.
Submetralhadora Bergmann Modelo 1938
Bergmann M38
During the late years of the Pessoa presidency, Brazil purchased a relatively small number of Bergmann MP28 submachine guns, but they never saw much use outside of national guard regiments in Rio itself; The M38 is a simplified and easily manufactured derivative of the MP28 created in response to growing tensions in South America, and was intended to be the standard issue firearm for the entire Brazilian military and was produced in large quantities in foundries across the country and as such became almost synonymous with the Brazilian military during the Weltkrieg period.
Mosquetão Semi-Automático Rossi Modelo 1944
As the Second Weltkrieg raged in Europe, Brazilian leadership found that their weapons were simply outmatched as the arms race between the great powers, and rather than try to catch up, it simply started producing an outright copy of the newest German semi automatic rifle designs such as the G41. The first models were made in the Rossi foundry in Rio Grande do Sul, wherein the model takes its name from. While more advanced than other weapons in use by the Paulista army, its low reliability made it unpopular with soldiers, who often preferred older models or even captured gear.
Rossi M44
Metralhadora M.08/15 & Morteiro de 7,58-cm
The Weltkrieg saw the introduction of some of the deadliest weapons known to man, such as the fearsome M.G. Modell 08/15. In the close confines of trench warfare, the once archaic mortar was brought back to relevance. Many of these older piece of equipment were among the hardware directly sold or leased to Brazil over the course of the military mission from Germany in that nation.
Metralhadora M34 & Morteiro de 8cm
The Machine Gun Model 34 (MG34) was a recoil operated air-cooled machine gun. Chambered in the powerful 7.92x57-mm Mauser rifle cartridge, the machine gun's high rate of fire (900 RPM) and efficient mobility made it arguably the most advanced machine gun in the world at the time; and was eagerly shown to Brazil as a proof of the martial superiority of the Kaiserreich. The perhaps unexpected consequence of that was the fact that the design was copied with little regard for patents by the Rio government after Black Monday. The Mortar Model 34 is an infantry mortar that employs 8-cm shells. It has been noted for its high accuracy and rate of fire.
Metralhadora M39 & Morteiro 'Torneira' de 20cm
The Machine Gun Model 39 (M.G. 39) was an improvement over the M.G. 34. This belt fed machine gun features a high rate of fire and is suited for all purposes. The 20-cm leichter Mortar Model 40 is a spigot mortar designed for striking obstacles and strong points. Brazilian copies were noted for having inferior quality materials in their fabrication, presumably to lower costs.
Metralhadora Imbel M1 & Morteiro de 8cm
The first models of heavy machine guns produced by Brazil, for Brazil, the Imbel models were noted for very high rate of fire, but also relatively low reliability and durability due to several corners cut during production. When it was working properly, it was one of the most fearsome weapons in the country's arsenal, however.
Metralhadora Anti-Tanque Imbel .50
The first models of heavy machine guns produced by Brazil, for Brazil, the Imbel models were noted for very high rate of fire, but also relatively low reliability and durability due to several corners cut during production. When it was working properly, it was one of the most fearsome weapons in the country's arsenal, however. Heavier variants were assigned to Anti Tank duties in the lack of proper weapons for the task in the armed forces.
Lança Rojão M44
The Model 44 Rocket Launcher, like many Brazilian weapons of its time, is a rather uninspired copy of European equipment used in the Second Weltkrieg, later produced and used by Brazil itself. Based mostly on the German 'Panzerschreck', the weapon shares most specifications with it, including its 8,8-centimetre rockets and the massive smoke trail left by firing.
Obuseiro Rheinmetall de 10,5 cm
After a series of military missions from and to Germany, Brazil's government started to import foreign artillery from that nation. These were Rheinmetall models were relatively modern for their time, but the nation had a very limited capacity for mass production of these at home. These guns were a significant upgrade from previous models used by Germany especially when it comes to hitting moving targets.
Obuseiro Modelo 41 de 11,5cm
The Obuseiro Modelo 41 was little more than a copy of the specifications of the Modell 36 field howitzer from the German army, but with some tweaks to lower production costs, at the expense of some reliability. Even so, the gun was extensively used by artillery in Brazil across the Weltkrieg period, and was the first piece of artillery mass produced domestically itself rather than being mostly imported.
Obuseiro Modelo 43 de 17cm
Still following the trend of copying specifications from German pieces of equipment, the 1943 update of the M41 had a slight increase in firepower, and some refinements with the intent of making it more reliable. However, production was limited during wartime, and the upgraded field gun was a rare sight over the early 1940s. In later years, however, it and models with minimal variations were used by the Carioca army until the 1960s.
Ob. Rm. de 10,5 cm
Ob. M41 de 11,5cm
Ob. M43 de 17cm
CAA M2 de 2cm
CAA M5 de 3,7cm
CAA M7 de 8,8cm
Canhão Antiaéreo M2 de 2cm
Anti Air weaponry was a defensive priority for Brazil, as the war between states had shown the vulnerabilities of the federal capital against aircraft despite extensive coastal and land based defences. Developed in conjunction and with support of Germany, the M1 and M2 were admittedly little more than copies of FlaK models from the early 1930s, but that was sufficient to deal with the relatively slow aircraft deployed in South America at the time.
Canhão Antiaéreo M5 de 3,7cm
As aircraft rapidly developed, several updates and changes to the standard issue M2 were made over the years, but later models of anti aircraft weaponry entirely different specifications regarding almost everything from the main axle to the size of the cannon itself. The M5 is closely related to its German cousin, the 3,7cm Fla.K 37, but is made of lower quality materials to meet the production needs of Brazil.
Canhão Antiaéreo M7 de 8,8cm
As aircraft rapidly developed, several updates and changes to the standard issue M2 were made over the years, but later models of anti aircraft weaponry entirely different specifications regarding almost everything, and the M7 is almost entirely a departure from the original design all but in role. The M7 was the first piece of anti aircraft equipment designed domestically, but even so it retained so many similarities to similar guns in use by Germany and its allies in the Weltkrieg many experts claim it wasn't a different gun at all, but rather a domestically produced variant. The cumbersome gun saw little use in Brazilian service before the war was over.
Canhão Antitanque 'Alemão' de 3,7 cm
Initially an outright import from Germany, the gun was straight up called 'Alemão' by the troops in the barracks due to its strength and obvious foreign origin, as its makers made sure to stamp imperial eagle effigies in seemingly every model. While similar models in Europe were designed to be drawn by motorised forces, Brazil used an outdated design more suited to the many horses it had available, and the lack of appropriate road infrastructure in an eventual frontline against Argentina. Said nation was the main motivator behind Brazil's move to start fabricating the piece domestically in small numbers after 1936, as the instability in that region, and having an unpredictable regime in possession of dozens of tanks, unnerved general staff in Rio.
Canhão Antitanque M2 de 7,5 cm
Developed entirely with German models as a basis, Anti Tank Artillery Model 2, or the AT2, was developed primarily against the types of heavier armour being used by European powers as the Second Weltkrieg raged. With Germany itself less than willing to cooperate with production this time, an illegally obtained piece was the basis for production domestically, which started much too late for widespread usage within the armed forces. The few models were usually distributed to divisions expected to face the burnt of enemy assaults.
Canhão Antitanque M6 de 12,8 cm
As the Weltkrieg came to a close, the armour in enemy Tanks became almost overbearing to infantry and older models of artillery alike, and Brazil's solution was yet again to mimic European designs in a cheap fashion. This domestic version of the Pa.K 43 has all of the problems of the original guns, but with lower reliability and was made with cheaper materials. Steel shortages were the main reason for the staggeringly low number of units produced during the war.
CAT Alemão de 3,7 cm
CAT de 7,5 cm
CAT M6 de 12,8 cm
Bateria Lança Foguetes de 32cm
Rocket artillery was rarely utilised by the Brazilian military during the war period, and the few pieces manufactured were direct copies of what little German equipment of the type Brazilian officers got their hands on. Following the specifications of the original models, rockets of 32cm were used in these weapons, and a lack of said rockets is exactly why they were seldom used.
Bateria Lança Foguetes de 21cm
Rocket artillery was rarely utilised by the Brazilian military during the war period, and the few pieces manufactured were direct copies of what little German equipment of the type Brazilian officers got their hands on. Changes to the size of the rockets required for usage made later models more common, but still far from standard issue and few pieces of the LF de 21cm were used in the field when compared to even the M43.
Bat. LF de 21cm
Bat. LF de 32cm

Pusca cu repetitie 'Mannlicher', model 1895
Mannlicher Md. 1895
The Mannlicher Model 1895 is a straight-pulled bolt action rifle designed by Ferdinand Ritter von Mannlicher that uses a more refined version of his revolutionary straight-pull action bolt. A staple in the armed conflicts of the Balkans and the Weltkrieg, numerous copies of the rifles exist in Romania's arsenals.
Pusca cu repetitie 'Zastava', model 1924
Zastava Md. 1924
Pistol-mitralieră 'Oriţa', model 1941
Oriţa Md. 1941
The Orita M1941 is a 9x19mm Parabellum submachine gun designed and manufactured in Romania. As tensions in the Balkans and Europe resurge, Romania has realised that it lacks automatic weapons and thus the Orita is a local attempt to create a weapon that would give Romanian infantry an edge in combat. Named after Captain Marin Orita (a captain in the Military Technical Corps), the weapon features an impressive rate of fire of 400-600 rounds per minute and fed through detachable 25/30 round magazines.
Pistol-mitralieră 'Oriţa', model 1942
Oriţa Carabină
The Orita Carbine fires the same 9x19mm Parabellum as the submachine gun but is a semi-automatic carbine variant. While the weapon maintains the fire-rate of a semi automatic rifle, it has been modified to maintain accuracy and reliability making it a deadly weapon in the hands of marksmen.
Puscă antitanc 'Mauser', model 1942
Mauser Md. 1942
The Model 1943 is a Mauser rifle converted to fire 15.2mm ammunition making it an effective anti tank weapon capable of penetrating the panzers of Austria.
Puscă antitanc 'Mauser', model 1943
Mauser Md. 1943
This revised version of the Model 1943 features reduced recoil and improved accuracy making it more reliable on the field than its predecessor.
Pistol-mitralieră 'MP', model 1928
MP Md. 1928
The MP28 is a German submachine gun, an evolution of the WK era MP-18 submachine gun. The gun is effective in close range and urban combat due to its size and rate of fire, making it ideal for trench combat. This iconic German submachine gun has found its way in Romanian hands especially among the Iron Guard.
Pistol-mitralieră 'MP', model 1940
MP Md. 1940
The M.P. 40, sometimes incorrectly called 'Schmeisser', was developed by Heinrich Vollmer and based on M.P. 38, with the aim of equipping German soldiers with an assault weapon. It uses magazines of 32 cartridges of 9mm, with its effective range being about 100-150 metres. It is a very reliable and particularly economical weapon, large numbers were sent to Romania.
Pistol-mitralieră 'Oriţa', model 1944
Oriţa Md. 1944
This variant of the Orita submachine gun comes with a folden metal stock and is made primarily for the Romanian special forces. This later version features a higher rate of fire than its predecessor as well as reduced recoil.
Mitralieră 'Maxim' Md. 1909 & 250 mm Mortier Negrei Md. 1916
Maxim Md. 1909 & 250 mm Negrei Md. 1916
Mitralieră 'Degtyarev' Md. 1929 & 82 mm Aruncător Md. 1938

Aruncător de flăcări 'Arges', model 1942
Arges Md. 1942
The Arges is a portable Romanian flamethrower adopted by the Romanian Land Forces. As incendiary mixture, it could use gasoline, petroleum, or H-E (a compound of gasoline and oil that appeared after the distillation of tar).
Autocamion 'RV', model 1935, Malaxa

-S
Vintovka obr.1891
Vintovka obr.1891
By 1936, the old Mosin rifle of 1891 has become an outdated, yet still reliable weapon. Compared with modern rifles, it is long and heavy. Most of these rifles have been converted to the new standard Mosin rifle of 1930.
Vintovka obr.1891/1930
Vintovka obr.91/30
The 1930 version Mosin rifle is shorter and lighter, originally based on the dragoon variant of the rifle. The new standard rifle of the Russian army is both lighter and more reliable with less moving parts than the old Mosin, while retaining its range and firepower.
Samozaryadnaya vintovka obr.1940
SVT
While the AVS was the first automatic rifle developed in Russia, the SVT by Tokarev was eventually adopted in its place as a more reliable option. Unlike the fully automatic AVS, which is largely relegated to usage by special forces and border troops, SVT-40 is only semi-automatic - but in this role it excels, and is perfectly comparable to its peers in other countries.
Avtomat (pistolet-pulemyot) obr.1943
PPSh-2
The PPSh-43, officially known as PPSh-2, is a development of its wildly successful predecessor, the submachine gun PPSh. It is generally cheaper and easier to maintain than its predecessor. Mass usage of submachine guns, enabled by rapid production of PPSh, have been adopted into the doctrine and tactics of Russian mobile infantry, based on experiences gained earlier in the war.
Pistolet-pulemyot obr.1934/1938
PPD-2
The PPD submachine gun family is the primary submachine gun of the Russian Army in the 1930s, but they lack a clear place in the military doctrine. Chiefly used as a weapon of officers and the military police, the technically complicated PPD-34/38 was recently adopted as a standard assault weapon of the Russian army, despite there not being a clear understanding of how to use this type of weapon in the future of warfare.
Avtomat (pistolet-pulemyot) obr.1941
PPSh
The PPSh-41 was accepted into the service as a replacement for PPD-34/38 as the primary submachine gun of the Russian Army after the formation of the Overwhelming Firepower Doctrine. It is easier to produce and maintain than the PPD, while having overall better performance. The gun is produced with two types of magazines - sectoral and drum-type, with the drum magazine being more common.
7,62-mm samozaryadny karabin obr.1945
SKS
The SKS is a development of Sergey Simonov's AVS rifle for the new 7.62 mm rounds, and it fixes many technical issues that were present in the original AVS. SKS is a semi-automatic battle rifle, and given its stellar performance, it is likely to eventually replace the SVT-40 entirely and become the main rifle of the Russian Army - at least until automatic rifles of the new generation are developed to an acceptable condition.
Protivotankovoye samozaryadnoye ruzhye obr.1941
PTRS
The PTRS and the less complex PTRD function as the main anti-tank rifles of the Russian Army. The PTRS is a self-loading rifle with a 5-round magazine, and despite its firepower, it is still merely an anti-tank rifle - and the experience has shown us how they have became increasingly outmatched against development of newer armour. Primary usage of the PTRS and PTRD has promulgated en masse - even if an individual AT rifle has only modest abilities, multiple fire-teams of experienced soldiers operating them will disassemble a tank piece by piece.
Protivotankovoye reaktivnoye ruzhye obr.1944
PTRO
The PTRO, developed by the team under Anatoly Ostrovsky's leadership, is an anti-tank reactive rifle developed to counter more modern armoured vehicles. The PTRO is bulky, unwieldy and requires two men to use it - but it is undoubtedly powerful, more so than comparable weapons in the west.
Stankovy pulemyot obr.1910 & 82-mm minomyot obr.1937
Maksim & 82-mm minomyot
The heavy firepower of Russian infantry battalion is focused on two weapons systems: the 1930 Maxim machine gun and a heavily modified version of the British 'Stokes' 82-mm mortar. While the Maxim is quite an old machine gun by modern standards, even despite its modifications, it will remain as the backbone of the Russian Army until the adoption of new infantry machine guns.
Stankovy pulemyot obr.1938 & 50-mm minomyot obr.1938
DShK & Osa
The DShK is a significantly heavier machine gun compared to the Maxim or the DP-27, and in addition to its calibre it is also compatible with anti-tank ammunition. The gun remains in sparse numbers due to its high price and complexity. As for infantry mortars, new 50-mm model Osa has been introduced as company level weapon to give every unit reliable fire support.
Ruchnoy pulemyot obr.1940 & 120-mm minomyot obr.1938
RD & 120-mm minomyot
The RD-40 (Ruchnoy, Degtyaryov) is a belt-fed universal machine gun and a replacement to the DP-27. It is a development on the earlier Degtyaryov, improving on firepower and overall performance, though it still remains somewhat inferior to German MGs. In addition, new heavier mortars based on the Stokes-Brandt 120-mm have been introduced as the new main mortar for the army, designed around mobility and reliability in an offensive war.
Stankovy pulemyot obr.1943 & 160-mm minomyot obr.1943
SG & 160-mm minomyot
The SG-43 is designed with the experience of the war as its direct guide. It is lighter and more reliable than the Maxim, seeking to fit the realities of modern, mobile war. At the same time, the further development of mortars has produced even greater calibres, as the need for heavier infantry support weapons has become especially pronounced in urban fighting in the Great Patriotic War.
Pribor Vega
Vega
The Vega series night-vision devices are binoculars designed specially for dark conditions. Depending on the version, its vision range varies from 150 m to 500 m, though the longest ranges are only possible with fixed naval versions named Omega. Being only the second generation of night vision devices, the Vega is still a very bulky and unreliable device, requiring infrared spotlights and heavy batteries with a limited charge.
Pribor Mira
Mira
The device Mira is a novel step for night vision devices. Officially labeled as 'goggles for soldiers', it consists of a pair of binoculars attached to a hat using a mounting system. However, the device is heavy, has to be attached to a power source, must utilise a separate infrared projector. Despite retaining many of the drawbacks of night vision technology, it is a respectable development in its field nonetheless.
Gruzovoy avtomobil AMO-F-15
AMO-F-15
The AMO-F-15 is based on the Italian Fiat 15, and was accepted as the main military truck of Russian Army in 1925. The F-15 was arguably already outdated then, and has been phased out in favour of AMO-3, which is based on American Autocar's designs, and was taken into the service in 1931. The F-15 remains reliable workhorse of the army, despite its age.
Gruzovoy avtomobil NAZ-63
NAZ-63
The NAZ-63 is a current-generation truck, based on the civilian NAZ-51 truck and purpose-designed as a proper all-wheeled military vehicle. It is reliable and can withstand most of the terrain and weather conditions encountered in Russia. It is often used together with its older brothers NAZ-AA and NAZ-MM, being the latest development of the NAZ truck family of reliable all-rounders.
Boyevaya avtoustanovka M-13
M-13
The M-13 is essentially an AMO-6 truck with an M-13 rocket launcher mounted on top. A full salvo of one truck contains sixteen 132-mm rockets, shot haphazardly and inaccurately, but with terrific effect when enough rockets are shot at the same section of the frontline.
Polugusenichny avtomobil AMO-42
AMO-42
The AMO-42 is the second widely adopted half-track in the Russian Army and is a modification of the earlier OKMO-VAN, fixing most of its predecessor's issues. This beast has the horsepower to draw even the heaviest artillery, and possesses the terrain capabilities to carry soldiers through any battlefield. It is not terribly fast, but it makes up the difference with reliability.
Bronetransporter B-42
B-42
The B-42 is a development of the AMO-42, inspired by German half-track models. It features sloped armour and can carry up to 14 soldiers, but yet still lacks in speed and is mired in technical issues.
Bronetransporter B-3
B-3
The B-3 is developed from the failed AT-3 artillery tractor, coupled with the lessons learned from B-42. The B-3 is a powerful and reliable engine of war, well-liked by the army, but its lacking speed and great weight leave something to be desired.
Plavayushchy traktor PBT-37
PBT-37
In preparation to the invasion of Eastern Europe, Russian engineers were tasked with developing an efficient river-crossing transporter. The PBT-37 is built on the chassis of the T-37, but with an amphibious drive, room for passengers copied from the failed OKMO-STB1, and thicker armour; naturally at the expense of firepower. This armoured tractor is designed for a single purpose-- crossing the Dniepr, Dvina and any other rivers standing between Russia and Berlin.
Bronetransporter PTR-20
PTR-20
An amphibious modification of the PT-20 tank, the PTR-20 is much heavier and larger than the PBT-37, capable of carrying greater loads. However, it is also not particularly maneuverable, and its amphibious capabilities are medicore at best. Despite that, the PTR-20 still does its job and can be used on a battlefield with minimal problem.
Legky broneavtomobil BA-20
BA-20
Based on the RB-2, the BA-20 is an improved version of OKMO's earlier armoured car models. It is cheap and reliable, though lacking in firepower, as it is chiefly used for recon.
Broneavtomobil BA-10
BA-10
The BA-10 is built on the basis of the NAZ-AAA with a reinforced chassis. It is considered to be a very successful model, with its decent speed, armament and with above-average plating for an armoured car.
Broneavtomobil BA-30
BA-30
The BA-30 is a modern replacement of the BA-20. It is armed with two light and one heavy machine guns, has high speed for its weight and strong armour for its role as a recon and support vehicle.
Broneavtomobil BA-12
BA-12
An improved version of the BA-11, the BA-12 has a diesel engine and is an especially reinforced vehicle for an armoured car. In a time when armoured cars were becoming less and less useful, the BA-12 was chiefly used as a light AT vehicle.
Parovoz serii Tk
Series Tk
The Tk is a modern train series intended to replace the older Series Э developed by the Kolomna factory. It is vastly more powerful as a locomotive, but is also much more complex to produce than the older trains.
Parovoz serii Ya
Series Ya
Series Ya is a complex upgrade to the old Series Э, stretching its capabilities to the maximum. It is somewhat weaker to the Series Tk, but vastly easier to produce and better fit to war-time conditions. They are essentially stripped of anything unnecessary to maintain their cheap production costs.
Bronepoyezd BP-41
BP-41
The BP-41 is a development of OKMO's OB-3. Equipped with sloped armour, proper armoured turrets unified with tanks, AA defence wagons, it is a veritably rationalised layout fit for dedicated military use. It might well become the last-- and the best-- proper war train, as the continued development of technology is rapidly leaving armoured trains behind.
Zheleznodorozhny transport TP
TP
The TP-1 is armed with a massive 356-mm railway gun, and is developed specifically for the army to simultaneously serve the role of stationary defensive and mobile offensive artillery support.
76-mm pushka obr.1933
F-19
The 76-mm F-19 is the main divisional gun for the Russian Army accepted into service as a temporary measure. It has become somewhat outdated and mediocre by the 1930s, but until a newer model can enter mass production, the F-19 will nonetheless form the backbone of Russian artillery.
76-mm pushka obr.1939
F-22
The 76-mm F-22 was developed by Vasily Grabin as an 'improvement' to the earlier rejected F-22, though despite those intentions, it is a completely new gun. The F-22 has proved to be a very dependable design, sometimes described as perfectly balanced in its capabilities, and due to that the gun became the reliable workhorse of the Russian artillery.
76-mm pushka obr.1942
F-43
The F-43 is another design by Vasily Grabin, intended to replace the old F-22s. The F-43 is light, easy to use, easy to produce - but as proof of its brilliant design, dispossessing real sacrifice in its combat capabilities.
152-mm mortira obr.1937
M-21
The 152-mm M1931 mortar licensed from Rhinemetall was further improved by Motovilikha to create the M-21. As a divisional mortar, the M-21 faces the difficult position of being neither powerful enough compared to divisional artillery nor widespread enough to serve as a direct support mortar, like its smaller calibre peers.
122-mm gaubitsa obr.1938
F-25
The F-25 is a proper modern divisional howitzer with a somewhat inadequate carriage. It has a 122-mm calibre and decent combat performance, but its true capability comes from the great numbers that it is commonly used in.
152-mm gaubitsa-pushka obr.1937
M-20M
The 152-mm M-20 howitzer is a corps level gun, and one of the best successes among the usually mediocre Russian howitzers. The F-20's carriage also serves as the core of several self-propelled guns. The Motovilikha's 152-mm howitzer is very versatile, being able to operate both direct and indirect fire. Despite having very powerful shells, it is relatively heavy and cumbersome to transport.
152-mm gaubitsa obr.1942
M-35
The 152-mm corps-level howitzer M-35 is a development of the Motovilikha's M-10. It is comparably light and manoeuvrable for a gun of its calibre, which distinguishes it from other high-calibre artillery.
45-mm protivotankovaya pushka obr.1937
53-P
The 53-P is a typical 1930s anti-tank gun: it has the relatively low calibre of 45-mm and while it works against lighter tanks, it is simply ineffective against heavier armour at a distance. The gun is also used as general battalion-level fire support.
57-mm protivotankovaya pushka obr.1941
F-40
The development of the 57-mm F-40 was hurried as part of Russian war planning, but despite this, it is considered to be a quality gun. The F-40 is a division-level gun, multi-purpose and liked by the soldiers, and is yet another one of Vasily Grabin's designs.
100-mm protivotankovaya pushka obr.1944
OF-63
The 100-mm Obukhov's OF-63 gun was designed in collaboration with Vasily Grabin to pierce even the heaviest tanks. It is used as a corps level anti-tank gun, and also as a gun for tank destroyers.
95-mm pushka obr.1939
F-28
The F-28 was developed for a shell that is unusual for Russia, so it was met with discontent in the artillery department. However, the gun attracted the attention of the tank forces, who decided to accept the gun in its tank version F-39. The 95-mm M1939 gun is partially unified with the F-25 howitzer and uses large-caliber shells that provide better penetration of tank armour.
45-mm protivotankovaya pushka obr.1942
M-6
The M-6 is a development of the 53-P, and despite technical improvements it is unable to pierce more modern armoured vehicles. It is chiefly used in large masses and at close range, where it still packs a significant punch.
85-mm protivotankovaya pushka obr.1943
F-53
The 85-mm F-53 is a further development of the 52-P anti-aircraft gun, adapted for anti-tank use. While the gun itself is almost never used by artillery forces due to problems with the carriage, tanks use it en masse due to the absence of this problem in its tank version. The gun is quite capable and can penetrate most types of armour from a good distance.
37-mm avtomaticheskaya zenitnaya pushka obr.1937
ASKOT
The main division-level anti-air gun, the 37-mm automatic ASKOT was developed by Kondakov's team in the mid-1930s. It has very high fire rate of 250 rounds per minute, but is known to be quite bulky and heavy due to its carriage.
25-mm avtomaticheskaya zenitnaya pushka obr.1940
72-P
The 25-mm 72-P is a regimental anti-air gun, significantly lighter than the ASKOT despite sharing its inconvenient carriage and being chiefly made for the immediate air defence of mobile units. It has a good fire rate and is reliable in field conditions, and can also be used as an improvised anti-tank gun wherever necessary.
85-mm zenitnaya pushka obr.1944
112-P
The heavy 85-mm 112-P anti-air gun is an upgraded version of the 52-P with better reloading speed and lower weight. It is used on a divisional level, and can also double as an anti-tank ordnance.
85-mm zenitnaya pushka obr.1939
52-P
The 85-mm 52-P is a replacement of the 3-P, and is a fundamentally modern high-calibre anti-air gun. Quick to reload and lighter than its predecessors, the 52-P fits the quicker pace of warfare that modern militaries engage in.
100-mm zenitnaya pushka obr.1940
73-P
The 100-mm 73-P is a heavy corps-level anti-air artillery which can also be used against armoured vehicles. Ultimately, the 73-P lacks true purpose, with corps-level anti-aircraft guns being used less and less as other types of anti-air weaponry have been improved.
25-mm avtomaticheskaya zenitnaya pushka obr.1944
94-P
The 94-P is another light, 25-mm anti-aircraft gun intended for regimental use. It is a development of the 72-P with paired barrels and a shield which serves as an effective rapid-fire multi-purpose gun.
Pekhotnaya ustanovka RS
M-8
The M-8 was developed as a portable infantry rocket launcher, and is among the first ones of its type. It is chiefly utilised by special forces, initially intended for mountain troops. The launcher fires 8 132-mm rockets with minimal requirements for position. Like any rocket system, it is inaccurate, heavy and very visible.
Puskovaya ustanovka M-31
M-31
The M-31 is a copy of the German approach - a rocket launcher installed on a carriage for better mobility. A single M-31 platform has 8 heavy 300-mm rockets, with good reloading speed due to its improved frame. It is inaccurate, but in large numbers can be used to devastating effect.
Reaktivny snaryad M-20
M-20
Based on the M-13 reactive round, the M-20 is a heavier and more powerful rocket of the same 132-mm calibre. The new round is used in the same quality as the M-13 and can be fired from the M-13 launchers.
Reaktivny snaryad M-30
M-30
The 300-mm M-30 reactive round is much more powerful than previous rockets, but needs different launchers due to its increased weight and size. Often called 'Luka' by soldiers due to its shape, the M-30 is one of the most devastating rockets produced by Russia.
Zheleznodorozhny transport TG
TG
The TG is a 500-mm railroad howitzer unified with the TP railway gun. Similar to the TP, it was developed specifically for the army, however unlike the TP gun it serves only the sole purpose of offence and cannot be dismounted.
203-mm gaubitsa obr.1931
O-4
The O-4 is one of the first and the most important Russian siege weapons developed after the end of the Great War. The gun is a part of the 'Big Artillery Triplex' and can destroy the vast majority of fortifications, except especially high-quality modern strongholds. It is a large, slow weapon with low reload speed and with a complicated, unreliable chassis that excels solely in destroying forts.
203-mm gaubitsa obr.1943
F-123
The F-123 is a modern siege weapon, but in its foundation lies a modified O-4 gun. A new chassis fixed the main issues of the O-4 gun, such as its ordinarily extremely low reload speeds.
Mototsikl AM-72
AM-72
Developed by OKMO in preparation for the war, the AM-72 is a modified copy of the German BMW R-71 motorcycle. It is easy to produce, reliable, easy to repair, and has solid speed and good manoeuvrability in harsh terrain. The AM-72 stands above other Russian motorcycles, which are either too light or too unreliable to be properly used by military.
Vertolyot V-4
V-4
Bombardirovshchik Zveno-7
Z-7
Bombardirovshchik TDB-1
TDB-1
Krylataya torpeda T-312
T-312
'The Winged Torpedo' is the first tactical missile developed by the Russian military. It has low accuracy and is comparatively weak in explosive power for its production costs, but it is still a significant pioneer in the field of Russian missile technology.
Raketa R-15
R-15
The two-stage R-15 rocket has high range, but still suffers from many of the same issues which plagued the T-312. It was developed by Langemak's team to serve as the main missile used by the Russian Army in the modern everchanging war on the basis of the civilian R-10 rocket.
Raketa R-2
R-2
The R-2 rocket is developed based on stolen German designs, and is essentially a Russian upgraded version of the V-2. The R-2 works by completely different principles than earlier Russian rockets.

Rifle, Short, Magazine, Lee-Enfield Mk III
SMLE Mk III
The venerable Lee-Enfield (SMLE) rifle that served the Empire throughout the Great War continues to be the standard arm of the Dominions following the Empire's collapse. Quantities of the SMLE rifle can be found in arsenal throughout the many Dominions. With rifle production seriously disrupted with the loss of the arms factories of England, the Dominions have turned to the old reliable three-oh-three as their standard weapon of choice until suitable replacements are created or purchased.
Rifle, Short, Magazine, Lee-Enfield Mk V
SMLE Mk V
After the fall of the Home Isles, the need to rearm what remained of the Empire became paramount. British engineers from the RSAF (Royal Small Arms Factory) began taking refuge in Ontario to work on an existing Lee-Enfield. The classic short magazine rifle's updated model displays a new and improved aperture system on the side instead of the middle, which features improved sighting radius, sighting accuracy, and sighting speed. However, due to the forging and machining operations required to construct the rifle, the production of this new SMLE design is relatively expensive.
Owen Mk 1
Owen Machine Carbine
With the prospect of war coming, the Army has requested a submachine gun to be developed for close quarters and urban warfare, especially with the destructiveness that characterises the civil war in America. The Canadian Army officially adopted a weapon designed by young Australian private Evelyn Owen. The \
Long Branch Mk 1
SLR Mk 1
The Crown Corporation Small Arms Ltd in Long Branch responded to requests from the Canadian government for a self-loading rifle. The self-loading rifle is chambered in 8mm Mauser cartridges and features a tilting bolt action. While the gun suffers from reliability issues and excessive recoil, the rifle comes with a shoulder pad to compensate for the recoil. In addition, the rifle's light weight makes it ideal for mobility and urban combat. Many copies were sent to arm the Dominions of the Empire in preparation for the eventual homecoming.
Receivers, Tabby, Periscope Mk 1
Tabby Scope
The Tabby Scope is one of the Canadian government's most closesly guarded secrets; the process of development is even hidden from the fellow members of the Entente. A chance discovery by scientists in the ISAC, the scope is shaped in the form of a canteen but contains a monocular infrared scope along with a battery. Assigned to only the most elite of the elite, the scope allows the unprecedented advantage of having vision in the dark.
BSA Thompson M1926
The Canadian Army has formally adopted the iconic American submachine gun associated with crime and vice. The M1928A1 is the service variant of the classic M1921 Thompson Machine gun, and although production is expensive, the gun is well-liked among the troops in the field who praise its efficiency and reliability. While most variants rely on smaller 'box' magazines, some other variants feature large and bulky fifty-round drum magazines.
Lanchester Submachine Gun
With the outbreak of all out war in the United States and the looming clouds of war in Europe, the Canadian Army desperately needs arms for the homecoming. With little time to prepare and research, the Canadian Army has commissioned the 'Lanchester' submachine gun, a near perfect copy of the German MP-28.
Canadian Machine Carbine Mk 1
In further cooperation with the Small Arms Ltd at Long Branch, the Canadian military has officially adopted a new compliment and perhaps successor to the Owen. The Machine Carbine Mk 1 features a selective fire trigger with an innovative horizontal magazine to withstand dirt, dust, and sand. Pressure on the top of the trigger would fire the weapon in fully automatic, while pressure on the bottom would fire semi-automatic. While the new machine carbine features a lower rate of fire than the Owen, its reliability and ability to deal selective fire make it quite the potential successor. Many quantities found their way into the arsenal of the Dominions.
Grenade, Rifle, Anti-tank No. 68
Witnessing a demonstration of Henry Mohaupt's anti-tank rifle grenade in Switzerland, a Canadian commission, guessing that the weapon used the shaped charge principle, began work on their own design. The resulting high-explosive anti-tank (HEAT) rifle grenade is hoped to provide greater capabilities for the infantry to fight enemy armour using the cup launchers already in service.
Projector, Infantry, Anti Tank Mk I
With the need for a hand-held anti tank weapon for use on the frontlines, the Projector, Infantry, Anti Tank Mk I (PIAT) has been developed based on the design of the bombard mortar. With an effective range of 105 metres in direct fire mode, the device has been well liked due to its lack of backblast - however there has been concerns about its intense recoil.
PIAT
Vickers MG & Stokes mortar
The water cooled Vickers MG and the Stokes trench mortar were the standard support arms of the Canadian Army during the Weltkrieg. With the threat of war ever so near, the Canadian Army has recommissioned them back into service.
Lewis Mk III DEMS & SBML two-inch mortar
With its iconic 'pan' magazine, the Lewis has served the Tommy since the darkest days of the First Weltkrieg. With the threat of war ever so near, the MKIII variant has a pistol grip that allows it to be fired from the shoulder on any part of a ship's deck. The SBML while small, is incredibly portable and has greater firepower and range than most rifle grenades.
Vickers M Mk II & ML 3 inch mortar
The Mark II variant of the Vickers MG features a selective fire option and a pistol grip. It has been primarily adopted for the armoured vehicles. The ML 3 inch mortar is a considerable upgrade from the Stokes, as it is reliable and sturdy for close artillery support.
Vickers M Mk III & ML 4.2 inch Mortar
The third variant of the esteemed Vickers machine gun was designed for anti-aircraft usage and features a slightly increased rate of fire from its predecessors. Likewise, the 4.2 inch mortar is a heavier upgrade of previous Canadian mortar models and capable of dropping intense and effective support.

Krag-Jørgensen Gevär M/89
Gevär M/89
Produced by the Mauser, the Gevär m/96 is a testament to Swedish engineering and military foresight. Chambered in the venerable 6.5x55mm cartridge, this bolt-action rifle has served Sweden with unmatched reliability. Its precision and durability make it a beloved tool among Swedish soldiers, ensuring its continued battlefield use. The m/96 remains a symbol of Swedish martial tradition, unaltered in its design and just as effective.
Mauser Gevär m/1932
Gevär m/32
Introduced in 1932, The Gevär m/32 continues to serve the Swedish armed forces with distinction. Its adoption, featuring slight modifications for improved ergonomics and accuracy, reflects Sweden's commitment to maintaining a formidable infantry force. Chambered in the efficient 6.5x55mm, the m/32 is a refined version of its predecessors, combining proven reliability with enhanced battlefield performance.\nNow with the creation of the Nordic Federation, the Rifle is now a standardized Rifle for the Federation.
Automatgevär m/1939
AG m/39
The AG m/39, or AG Pelo, was initially dismissed due to its complexity and cost, but due to the formation of the Nordic Federation, many Arms Designer across the federation assembled in Stockholm and they managed to make the long-recoil, semi-automatic rifle a reality. Chambered in 6.5x55mm, its adoption signifies Federation's innovative approach to modern warfare, providing its soldiers with a powerful tool that balances complexity with lethal efficiency.
Automatgevär m/1942
AG m/42
Building on the AG m/39's foundation, the AG m/42 introduced numerous enhancements that redefined its battlefield role. Incorporating a stainless-steel gas tube, ergonomic modifications, and a new 10-round detachable magazine, alongside other improvements, solidifies its status as a superior weapon. Chambered in the standard 6.5x55mm, the AG m/42 is a testament to Federation's adaptability and technological advancement, offering soldiers a reliable, powerful, and refined weapon for the challenges ahead.

Rifle No.1 Mk III

Rifle No.4 Mk I
No.4 Mk I
After the revolution and civil war it became apparent that the No.3 Enfield was not fit for urban combat. Trials for an entirely new rifle were finally held in 1932, but would largely fail to bear fruit, with new designs unable to match the old Enfield or receiving unfavourable troop evaluations. In light of this showing, Enfield replacement efforts were ultimately shelved. In 1935, however, a joint effort between The Revolutionary Small Arms factory in Enfield and Birmingham Small Arms was presented to the government. The new rifle was a development on the old Lee-Enfield with a shorter barrel, side mounted sling, and a simplified bolt system. While similar to its predecessors, the No.4 is stronger and easier to produce, though a bit heavier due to its barrel. An interesting fact about the No.4 is that it comes with an aperture sight that is set at increments of 100 yds (91m); calibrated for 200-1,300 yards (183-1189 metres).

Taiyuan Type 6-5 Infantry Rifle
Taiyuan Type 6-5
Made using foreign tooling imported to the Taiyuan Arsenal in 1925, this rifle is a close copy of the Japanese Type 38 rifle, and uses its original 6.5x50mm cartridge, which was also manufactured in the Arsenal.\n\nHowever, due to the turbulent reality of the period, tradional weaponry such as the Dadao sword was used alongside or instead of it by many a soldier.
Taiyuan Type 26
Taiyuan Type 26
Originally called the 'Type 27', this rifle was put into Qing service in 1935 through German assistance after the Restoration. The weapon is functionally a near copy of the German Mauser M1924, and a considerable improvement over the much older Type 88 in terms of weight and recoil.\n\nFirst produced at the Hanyang arsenal with German tools, manufacturing methods have already spread to Taiyuan, though it may not fully replace its predecessors for some time.
'Thampson' Model 1921 “Gezaolonglong”
'Thampson' M1921
Many Model 1921 Thompsons were imported into China during the 1920s, despite the USA being a leading adherent to an international embargo on the export of military weapons to that country. Copies were subsequently produced by at least three provincial arsenals. The Shanxi-made copies were stamped with the word 'Thampson' in misspelt recognition of the original designer and chambered to .45 ACP, resulting in ammunition shortage at one point due to its popularity.
Taiyuan Type 35
Taiyuan Type 35
The Type 35 is a semi-automatic rifle based on the General Liu rifle from 1914. While appearing similar, the Type 35 is shorter, has the rear of the receiver covered, and the gas-trap system replaced by a simple gas port. The new rifle is also no longer able to switch to manual action and uses magazines from the Bohemian ZH-29 rifle and ZB-26 light machine gun.

Shanxi Armoured Car
Zhuangjia Qiche
A batch of armoured vehicles modified from trucks by Yan Xishan's Xibei Locomotive Factory in Taiyuan. The exact number produced is unknown, but the total output is estimated to be more than 50 vehicles. The car is equipped with 1 to 3 light machine guns.
Shanxi Xinhai Type 26
Type 26
Yan Xishan's engineers soon imitated their own armoured vehicles after receiving covert military assistance from the Japanese. This armoured vehicle is a replica of the Japanese Type 92 armoured car, but the body design borrows some aspects from German armoured vehicles in the 1930s.
Jin Type Shanxi
Jin Type Shanxi
Due to their defeat in the Fourth Zhili-Fengtian War, Yan Xishan urgently needed a logistical military-purpose truck. Unfortunately, due to Shanxi's narrow roads and mountainous terrain, and the technical blockade imposed by the Qing government on Shanxi, it was difficult for Yan Xishan to buy trucks directly from the Japanese. Therefore, in March 1932, he ordered the engineer Jiang Shouting to go to Tianjin to negotiate with the representatives from the American Federal Motor Truck Company. The Americans eventually agreed to transfer the 1.5 ton truck technology to Shanxi, and Jiang Shouting used this as a basis to create the reliable and durable Type Shanxi by the end of the same year.

Puen Lek Yao Type 46/66 Siamese Mauser
PorLorYor.46/66
The Type 46/66 is a unique rifle, chambered in the Siamese 8x52mm Rimmed Cartridge, which incorporates what is essentially a hybrid Mauser 96 & 98 action into a body inspired by both Mauser and Arisaka designs. The Type 46 was the primary armament of the Siamese Forces during the Weltkrieg.
Puen Lek Yao Type 66 Siamese Mauser
PorLorYor.66
While strictly speaking, not truly a Mauser, the Type 66 is an upgraded Japanese export Type 38 Rifle with an action similar to that found on the older Siamese Type 46. It is chambered for the Siamese 8x52mm Rimmed Cartridge.
Puen Kol Muea Type 84 Siamese Submachine Guns
PorKorMor.84
The Type 84 is the Siamese license produced variant of the Bohemian ZK-383 submachine gun chambered in 9×19mm Parabellum. The Type 84 was adopted following Siam's decision to phase out the ageing MP-18; it was chosen both because it shared the 9x19mm catridge with the MP-18 and for its reliability in jungle conditions.
Puen Lek Yao Bunchuu-aeng Type 87 Semi-Automatic Rifle
PorLorYorBor.87
Inspired by the earlier success of Type 84 (ZK-383) SMG and the Type 66 (Madsen) LMG in the field, a local design team led by Maj. Gen. Vichian Suttantanon managed to successfully developed the first indigenous Semi-Automatic Rifle design. While the early prototypes proved to be problematic due to the lack of actual technical know-how, by the time it is adopted - the gun is well-liked by all troops it was issued to.

RSR 260 Hanomag
RSR 260
Ordered between 1928-1929 by the Royal State Railway of Siam, the RSR 260 was a class of 4-6-2 (Pacific) locomotive built by Hanomag. These locomotives, which superseded the existing E-Classes commissioned between 1915-1921, serve as the new workhorse of the expanding railway network in Siam for both express and mixed traffic trains.
RSR 350 Mikado
RSR 350
Also known as Japanese Government Railways DX50 locomotive, these locomotives imported from Japan were the first class of 2-8-2 (Mikado) that became successful within the Siamese service. The RSR later ordered more Mikado standard locomotives to meet railways as well as military demands.
RSR 350 Mikado HorKor.
RSR 350 HorKor.
As railways started to be attacked by enemy aircraft, new locomotives to serve on the fronts need to be able to take hits from up to 20mm cannons. To protect the locomotive for service against air attack, some RSR 350 Mikado locomotives are fitted with three-inch-thick armour plates along the locomotive to protect the vital parts.
Carcano Modello 1891
Carcano M91
The Carcan M91 was the standard rifle of the Italian armed forces during the Weltkrieg and the Italian Civil War. esigned by Salvatore Carcano at the Turin Army Arsenal in 1891, the carbine fires 6.5 x 52mm Carcano cartridges. The magazine system uses en bloc charger clips which were originally developed by Ferdinand Mannlicher - hence why the gun is often referred to as the 'Mannlicher-Carcano.'
Karabiner 98b
Mauser Kar. 98b
The Weltkrieg showed first-hand that full-length rifles were unwieldy in trench warfare with little benefit. Germany's famed assault troops were given the shorter Kar. 98AZ whenever possible, and soon after the war, it was decided to standardise on a carbine-length rifle to replace the G.98. The Kar. 98b, based on the AZ model, differed little from its direct predecessor, but more significantly from the longer G. 98, with improved sights and a turned-down bolt. More importantly, it used more parts from the long rifle to increase parts interchangeability and lower manufacturing costs. As part of Sicilian-German cooperation in response to the red threat of the north, large quantities of the 98b were shipped to Sicily.
SME M38
SME M38
Following the rejection of its 1938 pattern semi-automatic rifle, the CZ company attempted to market the design to a variety of foreign nations. The Two Sicilies tested the rifle and like the Austrians, found the rifle unreliable in harsh conditions and difficult to disassemble, but sought to redesign the gun to fix its shortcomings. The SME state run electrical company, which had begun to produce and design small arms only a few years prior, was set to the task. The end result, designated the SME M38 upon adoption, while improved over its Czech predecessor, still bears many of the latter's design quirks.

FS Gruppo 740
FS Gr. 740
Designed by the Adriatic Railways shortly before the nationalisation of the railways in 1905, the 740 Group is a series of 'Consolidation' class locomotives. Built to haul heavy trains on the mountainous lines of the Northern Appennine, while keeping a comparatively low axle load of 14 tons to run on older, less frequently mantained tracks, these engines excelled in their task, and were subsequently built in copious number before the Great War. Distributed across the Peninsula to relieve the older pre-nationalisation engines, a good number of those engines ended up in service in Sicily, and subsequently remained in our hands.
FS Gruppo 940
FS Gr. 940
Designed with the 740 Group as a basis, these 'Mikado' class tank engines were built to haul heavy freight trains on the steep lines of the Southern Appennines and the Rome-Pescara line. Though less powerful than their traditional engine-tender counterparts, they are overall more flexible and cheaper to operate, while their lower axle load allows them to run on older tracks.

Hanyang Type 88
Hanyang Type 88
Originally a product of late Guangxu era 'Self Strengthening' efforts, the Type 88 was designed as a close copy of the German Gewehr 88 with export modifications. While collectively inferior to newer rifles despite improvements, and often poorly maintained, the weapon is known to be rugged and reliable if unwieldy.\n\nThis variety is mainly produced at the Xining Arsenal in Qinghai, though equipment shortages and personal preference often see it used alongside non-standard weapons such as the Dadao.

Citroën P21 Type C6 'Croisière Jaune'
Citroën P21
In November 1931, the great Croisière Jaune (Yellow Expedition) organised by Citroën arrived in Xinjiang. Yang Zengxin, the governor of Xinjiang, was surprised by the French expedition across the Silk Road, and warmly received the expedition team. Seeing that these trucks can drive continuously in harsh environments, during the expedition's stay in Xinjiang, Yang Zengxin proposed to purchase a batch of Citroën P21 cars, and the expedition readily agreed to this request because the purpose of their expedition was to advertise for Citroën. Soon after the expedition arrived in Beijing in February 1932, the French shipped the first batch of auto parts and engineers to Xinjiang. This truck has also become the most common truck in Xinjiang.

Brzostrelka Model 1934
Steyr-Solothurn M.34
While a German design by Louis Stange, the  MP 34 was mainly produced by Steyr and was adopted by the Austro-Hungarian Army. As common with early submachine guns, this design was heavy, expensive, but reliable, with a horizontal magazine using the potent 9x25mm Mauser cartridge.
Brzostrelka Model 1938
Zbrojovka Brno M.38
Seeing the need for a submachine-gun using the standard pistol cartridge of the Army, the Monarchy would adopt the ZK 383, designed by brothers Josef and František Koucký at Zbrojovka Brno, as the MP 38. Using a horizontal magazine like the MP 34, the ZK 383 is known for having a light bipod, allowing it to be used as a substitute squad automatic weapon. Later models were heavily simplified for cheaper and faster production, along with a vertical foldable magazine like the Danuvia SMGs.
Brzostrelka Model 1943
Danuvia M.43
While the Danuvia 39M proved successful, its folding magazine was not enough to compensate for its bulky design for vehicle crewmen. The 43M redesign with a folding metal stock and a new, more reliable foldable magazine design allowed it to be much more compact during transport or storage, without sacrificing firepower.
