Karcan Nooc 1891
Carcano M91
Somalia's armed forces in the early 1930s had a variety of non standarized rifle models, but by far the most common, especially in Mogadishu and in the forces of the Hobyo was the Carcano rifle. Designed by Salvatore Carcano at the Turin Army Arsenal in 1891, the carbine fires 6.5 x 52mm Carcano cartridges. The magazine system uses en bloc charger clips which were originally developed by Ferdinand Mannlicher - hence why the gun is often referred to as the 'Mannlicher-Carcano', but in Somalia its also known as simply the 'Karcan', and large amounts of the gun were in use by native Askari and colonial troops alike during their disorganised withdrawl at the tail end of the Weltkrieg, wherein much material was left behind.
Kirkale Nooc 55
Kirkale Q55
The initial standardisation and modernisation efforts for the military in Somalia were based greatly on the Ottoman Empire, as the two nations enjoyed quite amicable relations in the 1930s. Starting in 1933, the Ottoman Empire updated their old rifles to a common configuration known in the Empire as the Model of 1936 and all in 8x57 Mauser cartridge. Many of these weapons were sold to Somalia, as the state had a difficult time establishing a local manufacturing plant for weapons. As the years went by, Somalia copied the 55 model (Named after its model Hegira Year) and made a respectable amount of domestic versions, usually quite inferior to Turkish and German equivalents.
Rayfal Soomaali Nooc 61
RSN1.61
As the Ottoman strategic concerns turned towards arming their own Empire, Somalia found itself somewhat lacking in willing trade partners in the Middle East, and really Europe as a whole, in terms of weapons trade. The Model 61 was for all intents an unauthorized liscenced copy of the Kirikkale T60 which saw limited usage, but retains symbolic importance as the first firearms made and designed within the modern Somali nation.
Rayfal Soomaali Nooc 65
RSN2.65
The Model 65 saw extended use in the post-war era in Somalia, too few of the model were deployed to be truly relevant in the wars the nation found itself during said timeframe. It's semi automatic design was very obviously inspired by German weaponry, but in its finer details it's closer to Turkish models of the same timeframe, as the Red Sea was flooded with Ottoman war material after the Levantine War.
Espingarda Mauser Modelo 1908
Mauser M08
The Mauser Model 1908 was an exceptionally long rifle based on the Mauser 1898 and chambered in 7x57mm Mauser. It was originally produced for Brazil by the German company DWM, but Brazil has subsequently begun to produce staggering quantities of the rifle domestically, and it became a staple in many state armies as time went it became almost synonym with the Interstate War in the cultural mindset of the nation. The São Paulo state's army used the same gear as the other states that formed Brazil, and alongside the southern states it was the premier fighting force of the region.
Fusil Mauser Modelo 1935
Mauser M35
The Mauser Rifle Model 1935 is a unique Mauser Rifle which utilises a 7x57mm cartridge produced domestically by Brazil and abroad in close conjunction with the Mauser company, as part of the extensive collaboration between the Brazilian and German governments. Said collaboration started in the 1910s, as a clique officers then derided as 'the Young Turks' by the press began lobbying extensively for closer cooperation with the global hegemon. Everything from helmets to artillery pieces started to be fashioned after the German model, and as such a modernisation of the older Mausers became a priority. This firearm became almost synonymous with the Brazilian military during the Weltkrieg.
Submetralhadora Bergmann Modelo 1938
Bergmann M38
During the late years of the Pessoa presidency, Brazil purchased a relatively small number of Bergmann MP28 submachine guns, but they never saw much use outside of national guard regiments in Rio itself; The M38 is a simplified and easily manufactured derivative of the MP28 created in response to growing tensions in South America, and was intended to be the standard issue firearm for the entire Brazilian military and was produced in large quantities in foundries across the country and as such became almost synonymous with the Brazilian military during the Weltkrieg period.
Mosquetão Semi-Automático Rossi Modelo 1944
As the Second Weltkrieg raged in Europe, Brazilian leadership found that their weapons were simply outmatched as the arms race between the great powers, and rather than try to catch up, it simply started producing an outright copy of the newest German semi automatic rifle designs such as the G41. The first models were made in the Rossi foundry in Rio Grande do Sul, wherein the model takes its name from. While more advanced than other weapons in use by the Paulista army, its low reliability made it unpopular with soldiers, who often preferred older models or even captured gear.
Rossi M44
Metralhadora M.08/15 & Morteiro de 7,58-cm
The Weltkrieg saw the introduction of some of the deadliest weapons known to man, such as the fearsome M.G. Modell 08/15. In the close confines of trench warfare, the once archaic mortar was brought back to relevance. Many of these older piece of equipment were among the hardware directly sold or leased to Brazil over the course of the military mission from Germany in that nation.
Metralhadora M34 & Morteiro de 8cm
The Machine Gun Model 34 (MG34) was a recoil operated air-cooled machine gun. Chambered in the powerful 7.92x57-mm Mauser rifle cartridge, the machine gun's high rate of fire (900 RPM) and efficient mobility made it arguably the most advanced machine gun in the world at the time; and was eagerly shown to Brazil as a proof of the martial superiority of the Kaiserreich. The perhaps unexpected consequence of that was the fact that the design was copied with little regard for patents by the Rio government after Black Monday. The Mortar Model 34 is an infantry mortar that employs 8-cm shells. It has been noted for its high accuracy and rate of fire.
Metralhadora M39 & Morteiro 'Torneira' de 20cm
The Machine Gun Model 39 (M.G. 39) was an improvement over the M.G. 34. This belt fed machine gun features a high rate of fire and is suited for all purposes. The 20-cm leichter Mortar Model 40 is a spigot mortar designed for striking obstacles and strong points. Brazilian copies were noted for having inferior quality materials in their fabrication, presumably to lower costs.
Metralhadora Imbel M1 & Morteiro de 8cm
The first models of heavy machine guns produced by Brazil, for Brazil, the Imbel models were noted for very high rate of fire, but also relatively low reliability and durability due to several corners cut during production. When it was working properly, it was one of the most fearsome weapons in the country's arsenal, however.
Metralhadora Anti-Tanque Imbel .50
The first models of heavy machine guns produced by Brazil, for Brazil, the Imbel models were noted for very high rate of fire, but also relatively low reliability and durability due to several corners cut during production. When it was working properly, it was one of the most fearsome weapons in the country's arsenal, however. Heavier variants were assigned to Anti Tank duties in the lack of proper weapons for the task in the armed forces.
Lança Rojão M44
The Model 44 Rocket Launcher, like many Brazilian weapons of its time, is a rather uninspired copy of European equipment used in the Second Weltkrieg, later produced and used by Brazil itself. Based mostly on the German 'Panzerschreck', the weapon shares most specifications with it, including its 8,8-centimetre rockets and the massive smoke trail left by firing.
Obuseiro Rheinmetall de 10,5 cm
After a series of military missions from and to Germany, Brazil's government started to import foreign artillery from that nation. These were Rheinmetall models were relatively modern for their time, but the nation had a very limited capacity for mass production of these at home. These guns were a significant upgrade from previous models used by Germany especially when it comes to hitting moving targets.
Obuseiro Modelo 41 de 11,5cm
The Obuseiro Modelo 41 was little more than a copy of the specifications of the Modell 36 field howitzer from the German army, but with some tweaks to lower production costs, at the expense of some reliability. Even so, the gun was extensively used by artillery in Brazil across the Weltkrieg period, and was the first piece of artillery mass produced domestically itself rather than being mostly imported.
Obuseiro Modelo 43 de 17cm
Still following the trend of copying specifications from German pieces of equipment, the 1943 update of the M41 had a slight increase in firepower, and some refinements with the intent of making it more reliable. However, production was limited during wartime, and the upgraded field gun was a rare sight over the early 1940s. In later years, however, it and models with minimal variations were used by the Gaucho army until the 1960s.
Ob. Rm. de 10,5 cm
Ob. M41 de 11,5cm
Ob. M43 de 17cm
CAA M2 de 2cm
CAA M5 de 3,7cm
CAA M7 de 8,8cm
Canhão Antiaéreo M2 de 2cm
Anti Air weaponry was a defensive priority for Brazil, as the war between states had shown the vulnerabilities of the federal capital against aircraft despite extensive coastal and land based defences. Developed in conjunction and with support of Germany, the M1 and M2 were admittedly little more than copies of FlaK models from the early 1930s, but that was sufficient to deal with the relatively slow aircraft deployed in South America at the time.
Canhão Antiaéreo M5 de 3,7cm
As aircraft rapidly developed, several updates and changes to the standard issue M2 were made over the years, but later models of anti aircraft weaponry entirely different specifications regarding almost everything from the main axle to the size of the cannon itself. The M5 is closely related to its German cousin, the 3,7cm Fla.K 37, but is made of lower quality materials to meet the production needs of Brazil.
Canhão Antiaéreo M7 de 8,8cm
As aircraft rapidly developed, several updates and changes to the standard issue M2 were made over the years, but later models of anti aircraft weaponry entirely different specifications regarding almost everything, and the M7 is almost entirely a departure from the original design all but in role. The M7 was the first piece of anti aircraft equipment designed domestically, but even so it retained so many similarities to similar guns in use by Germany and its allies in the Weltkrieg many experts claim it wasn't a different gun at all, but rather a domestically produced variant. The cumbersome gun saw little use in Brazilian service before the war was over.
Canhão Antitanque 'Alemão' de 3,7 cm
Initially an outright import from Germany, the gun was straight up called 'Alemão' by the troops in the barracks due to its strength and obvious foreign origin, as its makers made sure to stamp imperial eagle effigies in seemingly every model. While similar models in Europe were designed to be drawn by motorised forces, Brazil used an outdated design more suited to the many horses it had available, and the lack of appropriate road infrastructure in an eventual frontline against Argentina. Said nation was the main motivator behind Brazil's move to start fabricating the piece domestically in small numbers after 1936, as the instability in that region, and having an unpredictable regime in possession of dozens of tanks, unnerved general staff in Rio.
Canhão Antitanque M2 de 7,5 cm
Developed entirely with German models as a basis, Anti Tank Artillery Model 2, or the AT2, was developed primarily against the types of heavier armour being used by European powers as the Second Weltkrieg raged. With Germany itself less than willing to cooperate with production this time, an illegally obtained piece was the basis for production domestically, which started much too late for widespread usage within the armed forces. The few models were usually distributed to divisions expected to face the burnt of enemy assaults.
Canhão Antitanque M6 de 12,8 cm
As the Weltkrieg came to a close, the armour in enemy Tanks became almost overbearing to infantry and older models of artillery alike, and Brazil's solution was yet again to mimic European designs in a cheap fashion. This domestic version of the Pa.K 43 has all of the problems of the original guns, but with lower reliability and was made with cheaper materials. Steel shortages were the main reason for the staggeringly low number of units produced during the war.

Bateria Lança Foguetes de 32cm
Rocket artillery was rarely utilised by the Brazilian military during the war period, and the few pieces manufactured were direct copies of what little German equipment of the type Brazilian officers got their hands on. Following the specifications of the original models, rockets of 32cm were used in these weapons, and a lack of said rockets is exactly why they were seldom used.

Rocket artillery was rarely utilised by the Brazilian military during the war period, and the few pieces manufactured were direct copies of what little German equipment of the type Brazilian officers got their hands on. Changes to the size of the rockets required for usage made later models more common, but still far from standard issue and few pieces of the LF de 21cm were used in the field when compared to even the M43.

Tipo 1933
T-33
The Type 1933 is the culmination of a long series of designs by the Trubia company based loosely upon the Renault FT. While the company's earlier 1925 model was field tested by the Spanish army, the 1933 was the first domestically designed tank to be formally adopted by the Spanish military.
Tipo 1936
T-36
Designed by a military bureau from the ground up, not on the basis of any other vehicle, the Type 1936 was a substantial improvement over earlier Spanish designs. While its 20mm Breda main cannon was disliked by troops, the vehicle was otherwise reliable and well-received.
Tipo 1941 'Verdeja'
T-41 'Verdeja'
The Type 1941 was the most successful design by young Major Félix Verdeja Bardales. The vehicle was designed with special consideration for the protection of its engine bay, and featured a domestically designed 45mm main cannon.

Mauser C96 “Boke Qiang”
Boke Qiang
The Mauser C96 (Construktion 96) is a semi-automatic pistol that was originally produced by German arms manufacturer Mauser from 1896 to 1937. Unlicensed copies of the gun were also manufactured in Spain and China in the first half of the 20th century. The gun itself was known as 'Boke Qiang'(scorpion gun) as it saw widespread usage during the warlord era, though equipment shortages and personal preference often see it used alongside non-standard weapons such as the Dadao.
Jinan Type 26
Jinan Type 26
Originally called the Type 27', this rifle was put into Qing service in 1935 through German assistance after the Restoration. The weapon is functionally a near copy of the German Mauser M1924, and a considerable improvement over the much older Type 88 in terms of weight and recoil.\n\nFirst produced at the Hanyang arsenal with German tools, manufacturing methods have already spread to Jinan, though it may not fully replace its predecessors for some time.
Taiyuan Arsenal  Type 20 “Zilaide”
Zilaide
An improvement to the original Mauser C96 Design, the M1932 Schnellfeuer (Rapid Fire), or as known as 'Zilaide' in Chinese was a very successful design with detachable magazine-fed and select-fire capability.\n\nFurther improvement in the later versions included a detachable barrel, improved front and rear sights, more durable parts to prevent breakage under sustained fire and lowered position of the shoulder stock to avoid 'hammer bite'.
Hanyang  Type 35
Hanyang Type 35
The Type 35 is a semi-automatic rifle based on the General Liu rifle from 1914. While appearing similar, the Type 35 is shorter, has the rear of the receiver covered, and the gas-trap system replaced by a simple gas port. The new rifle is also no longer able to switch to manual action and uses magazines from the Bohemian ZH-29 rifle and ZB-26 light machine gun.

$GER_night_vision$

Carcano Modello 1891
Carcano M91
The Carcano M91 was the standard-issue bolt action rifle of the Italian Army during the Weltkrieg. Often mistakenly called the Mannlicher-Carcano, the rifle's magazine uses en bloc charger clips initially from Ferdinand Mannlicher, but the actual shape and design of the Carcano clip come from the German Model 1888. As the royal family fled from the peninsula to Sardinia in haste, these rifles will have to do to defend Sardinia from godless revolutionaries.
Fucile Semi-Automatico Enfield
Fucile Enfield
As Sardinia lacks heavy military industry, it relies on weapons from the other Entente powers. The Enfield-Ontario (designed by the Canadian Army) is a gas-operated semi-automatic conversion of the classic SMLE rifle. Even if Sardinia cannot produce her arms, the Entente is more than happy to help.
Carabina automatica Hotchkiss
Carabina Hotchkiss
A weapon of National French origin, large quantities of the Carabina automatica Hotchkiss were shipped to Sardinia. The Carabina is an ambitiously-engineered and well-built submachine gun submitted by Hotchkiss in 1938 as the Type 017, which entered service as the Carabine-Mitrailleuses Hotchkiss Type M2 (along with its police variant Type M1). The CMH2's extreme compactness is both its best and worst feature - the complexity of having every protruding part fold or retract make the weapon expensive to produce and also reduces ergonomics, which isn't ideal for quick target acquisition.
Fucile Automatico MAS Modello 1943
Fucile Automatico M1943
Like most of Sardinia's arsenal, the Fucile Automatico MAS modello 1943 is a French weapon. The Fusil MAT Modèle 43 is an automatic rifle, using a 7.5x54mm cartridge and a foldable magazine, which allows it to be a little more compact than its regular counterparts. Along with this, the MAT-43 is produced by machine-stamping process which allows the economical production of large numbers of rifles, then urgently required by the Sardinian Government. Despite some issues with rate of fire and reliability, the MAS-43 is considered as the next step in personal weapons.
Darne M1919 & Stokes mortar
The Darne M1919 is a machine gun of French origin. The weapon's appearance is crude and the belt fed monster of a machine gun was designed for rapid manufacturing technologies due to the exile of so many Frenchmen. The Stokes mortar is a Weltkrieg era British smoothbore trench mortar that allows for higher angles of fire.
Mitrailleuse Hotchkiss Mle 1926 & Mortier Brandt Mle 27/31
Hotchkiss Mle 1926 & Brandt Mle 27/31
The Hotchkiss Mle 1926 is a machine gun of French origin, adopted formally by the Sardinian military. It is a light machine gun with a regulator that controlls the rate of fire as well as an overhead or belt fed magazine. The simple and effective Brandt mortar designed by Edgar Brandt requires a ten man crew and can fire off 18 rounds per minute making it an incredible weapon for supporting fire.
Mitrailleuse Hotchkiss Mle 26/37 & Mortier Brandt Mle 35/38
Hotchkiss Mle 26/37 & Brandt Mle 35/38
As tensions grow across the continent, the Entente must be ready to begin plans for the homecoming. New adjustments and refinements have been made to the Hotchkiss Mle that reduces the machine gun's recoil while slightly increasing its rate of fire.
Mitrailleuse Hotchkiss Mle 26/41 & Mortier Brandt Mle 1942
Hotchkiss Mle 26/41 & Brandt Mle 42
The continued use of the Hotchkiss machine gun and Brandt mortar reflects the close Franco-Sardinian cooperation. The latest version of the Hotchkiss features an increased rate of fire and telescopic sights for improving accuracy while the latest version of the Brandt mortar features an increased range and rate of fire as its predecessors.
Carabina Modello 1928
As part of Sardinia's cooperation with the Entente, the Sardinian forces have adopted the Canadian M1928A1. The M1928A1 is the service variant of the classic M1921 Thompson Machine gun, and although production is expensive, the gun is well-liked among the troops in the field who praise its efficiency and reliability. While most variants rely on smaller 'box' magazines, some other variants feature large and bulky fifty-round drum magazines.
Lanchester Submachine Gun
The Lanchester is a submachine gun of Canadian origin, a near carbon copy based on the German MP28. As part of Anglo-Sardinian cooperation, copies of the Lanchester were sent to Sardinia as they lack in submachine guns in quantity.
De Lisle Carbine
The De Lisle Carbine is an advanced silenced rifle that helps the user maintain accuracy as well as stealth. To aid Sardinian special forces, the Canadians sent copies of the De Lisle - a reflection of the Entente's continued support for Sardinia.
Cannone da 75mm Modello 1897
Cannone da 75mm
The Matériel de 75mm Mle 1897, also known as the French 75 or 'Soixante-Quinze' ('seventy-five'), is widely regarded as the first modern artillery piece. In service since 1898, the Soixante-Quinze was heavily used in the Weltkrieg, where it was used as an anti-personnel, anti-aircraft and anti-tank weapon. After the retreat to Algeria, the French army continued to use these weapons, mainly because they still mostly meet modern criteria.
Obice da 105mm Modello 1935 Schneider
Obice da 105mm S
The Matériel de 105mm Court Mle 1935 is a conservative design by Schneider. Developed to replace Soixante-Quinze in service, the Matériel de 105mm is more a howitzer than a cannon, and is primarily intended to destroy enemy fortifications.
Cannone da 155mm Grande Potenza Filloux Modello 1917/1942
Cannone da 155mm GPF
The Canon de 155mm Grande Puissance Filloux Modèle 1917, also known as the GPF, was developed during the Weltkrieg by Colonel Louis Filloux to meet the urgent need for modern heavy artillery, and is used by both the Communard and the National governments. Due to problems with the production of GPFs in the colonies by the French government, only a limited numbers were in service until 1942, when the GPF design was updated to facilitate production and meet modern standards.
Cannone da 25mm Semiautomatico Modello 1934
Cannone da 25mm SA
By the early 1920s, the French Army had come to the realisation that the armour-piercing capability of the 37mm TRP infantry gun would be insufficient against modern tanks. In 1926 Hotchkiss proposed a 25mm gun design, which was not immediately adopted due to financial issues, and the availability of the Matériel de 75mm. The Matériel de 25mm, which entered service only in 1936 with the realisation of the approaching battle for France, is a reliable weapon inspired by the Filloux concept.
Cannone controcarro da 75mm Modello 1897/1937
Cannone da 75mm CC
With the adoption of the Matériel de 105mm, the old Matériel de 75mm were mainly redesigned into anti-tank guns with an updated chassis. Considered too heavy for modern anti-tank guns, the Soixante-Quinze have higher penetration than their counterparts.
Cannone controcarro da 75mm Semiautomatico Modello 1943
Cannone da 75mm CC SA
The Matériel de 75mm SA is a new semi-automatic gun based on the 75mm Matériel de 75mm AC cannon. With a higher rate of fire, the Matériel de 75mm CA SA is still a slightly outdated weapon, but can compete with its modern counterparts, thanks to a modernised mechanism and a new approach to the chassis design.
Cannone-Mitragliera da 25mm contraerea Modello 1936
Cannone-Mitragliera da 25mm CA
After the retreat to Algeria, the French military announced the need for a specialised anti-aircraft autocannon. Hotchkiss introduced the 25 mm project in 1936, which was adopted due to the slow development of a more promising Schneider variant. Despite the acceptance of the Mitrailleuse 25mm CA into service, the original tripod was replaced to a triangular base with a two-wheel carriage as per the army's request.
Cannone-Mitragliera da 37 mm contraerea Modello 1939
Cannone-Mitragliera da 37mm CA
Developed since 1930, the Mitrailleuse 37mm CA was finally ready for production in 1939. After a bitter controversy with the French military, who had already adopted the Hotchkiss variant, the Mitrailleuse 37mm CA from Schneider was adopted after initial testing as a more advanced variant than the Hotchkiss's 25mm gun.
Cannone da 75mm contraerea Modello 1940
Cannone da 75mm CA
During the late 1920s, it was realised that the Matériel de 75mm Modèle 1897 was outdated as an anti-aircraft weapon and development of a new gun was begun in 1931. The Matériel de 75mm Contre-Aérien Modèle 1940 by Schneider has faster rate of fire, higher muzzle velocity, increased vertical range, modern fire control and greater mobility with new gun carriages, than the old Soixante-Quinze. Impressed by the performance of the former Mitrailleuse 37mm CA from Schneider, the French command quickly adopted the new 75mm gun.

FS Gruppo 740
FS Gr. 740
Designed by the Adriatic Railways shortly before the nationalisation of the railways in 1905, the 740 Group is a series of 'Consolidation' class locomotives. Built to haul heavy trains on the mountainous lines of the Northern Appennine, while keeping a comparatively low axle load of 14 tons to run on older, less frequently mantained tracks, these engines excelled in their task, and were subsequently built in copious number before the Great War. Distributed across the Peninsula to relieve the older pre-nationalisation engines, a good number of those engines ended up hauling trains on the Sardinian Dorsal Railway, and subsequently remained in our hands.
FS Gruppo 741
FS Gr. 741
Designed with the scarcity of vital resources such as coal in mind, the 741 Group is an evolution of the 740 Group including various improvements, such as the new Caprotti valve gear and the Franco-Crosti boiler. Vastly cheaper to run and more powerful than most other locomotives, the 741 Class does have a higher axle load than their predecessors, making it more difficult to run such engines on older tracks.

Carcano Modello 1891
Carcano M91
The Carcano M91 was the standard issue rifle of the Italian soldier during the Weltkrieg. Designed by Salvatore Carcano at the Turin Army Arsenal; the Carcano M91 served the Italian infantrymen during the Weltkrieg and the Civil War. With the threat of the continuation of the conflict ever so present, the Carcano M91 once again has been pushed back into service.
MAS Modèle 1936
MAS-36
The MAS 36 is a French short carbine-style rifle with a two-piece stock and slab-sided receiver. Built-in the Commune of France, many MAS-36 rifles arrived in the Socialist Republic of Italy to aid the revolutionary cause on the Italian peninsula. An economical and simple bolt action rifle, the MAS-36 is a handy and deadly weapon in the right hands.
MAS Modèle 1938
MAS-38
The MAS Modele 1938 is a submachine gun of French origin. Yet another successful weapon developed by MAS, the MAS Modele 1938 in Italian service reflects the increasingly closer ties and cooperation between the Commune of France and Socialist Republic of Italy. A high quality weapon with a firing rate of 600-700 rpm, the MAS 38 will give an edge to Italian soldiers fighting in urban or close quarters combat.
Fucile Armaguerra Mod. 39 Rifle
Armaguerra Mod.39
The Fucile Armaguerra Mod.39 is an Italian semi-automatic rifle. Developed by Gino Revelli (the son of the famed Abiel Bethel Revelli, known for the Fiat-Revelli machine gun and Glisenti Model 1910 pistol), the weapon was built by the Società Anonima Revelli Armiguerra in Genoa. The weapon got its name from the Telegraphic Code of Company, Armaguerra. A weapon with important accuracy and reliability, the Armaguerra will help bring the revolution to a successful finish.
Fiat-Revelli Modello 1914 & Brandt Mortar
The Fiat-Revelli Modello 1914 is a weapon from the Weltkrieg and Civil War. A powerful machine gun, the weapon has been brought back into service due to a lack of Italian machine guns and the growing tensions on the Italian boot. The Brandt mortar is a relic from the Weltkrieg, a refinement of the British 'Stokes' trench mortar. A simple and effective weapon, the mortar can be dissembled into three parts and requires a crew of ten.
Fiat-Revelli Modello 1936 & Brandt Mle 27/31
The Fiat-Revelli Modello 1936 is a modified version of its 1914 predecessor. The Modello 1936 features a more conventional belt-feed and aircooling and a steady rate of fire of 600 rounds per minute.
Chatelleraut FM Mle 24/29 & Brandt Mle 35/38
The Chatelleraut FM Mle 24/29 is a machine gun of French origin that has been sent to Italian military service due to a lack of heavy weapons. While the Chatelleraut features a low fire rate, it is a robust and reliable weapon; well-liked by our troops for its consistency and weight. The Brandt Mle 35 is a 60mm mortar to be used by infantry companies for indirect fire. Simple and effective, it only requires a crew of five to operate.
MAS AA-42 & Brandt Mle 1942
Experience in the Second Weltkrieg has led to an interest in general purpose machine guns to serve a variety of tactical roles. With nearly double the rate of fire of the Chatelleraut, the AA-42 is a belt-fed monster that will mow down anything in its path. The Mle 42 is a considerable improvement over its predecessor, with an emphasis on a greater close quarters support weapon.
Canon de 75mm mle 1897 modifee 1933
The French field gun developed for anti personal usage has been placed into Italian service. While maintaing the shield and wheels of the original field gun, this variant has increased elevation and a 58 degree traverse.
LRAC de 73mm Mle 1943
An anti-tank rocket launcher, the LRAC can fire a 73mm high explosive antitank projectile capable of penetrating over 11 inches of rolled homogenous armour. With the lack of heavy Italian weapons, the LRAC is a weapon of French origin. The LRAC has a shield to protect the operator from the rocket's back blast.
OVP 1938
The OVP 1938 is a submachine gun of Italian origin. The weapon is one half of the Villar-Perosa submachine gun. The gun features a delayed blowback and selective fire while being able to dish out 900 rounds per minute making it an absolute butcher in close quarters.
MAS-36 LG39
As part of the Franco-Italian cooperation, the SRI has access to the latest weapons from the Commune of France. This variant of the MAS-36 comes equipped with a folding hollow aluminium stock and strengthened barrel. It can also be used for grenade launching purposes as it comes with a 48mm grenade launcher.
CEAM Modele 1944
An assault rifle of French origin, the CEAM Modele 1944 is the latest weapon to emerge from the arms factories of the Commune of France. Copied from German designs, the use of such an advanced weapon gives the SRI an unprecedented advantage over its rivals on the peninsula.

FS Gruppo 625
FS Gr. 625
Designed in two batches by the Adriatic Railways in 1903 and the National Railways in 1909, the 625 Group are 'Mogul' class multirole engines built in Germany before the Great War. These engines were equipped with the 'Italian Bogie', a special frontal bogie designed to run on low radius bends on older lines, as well as the Caprotti valve gear. With the Northwestern lines and the Porrettana line between Bologna and Florence being rapidly electrified in the three-phase AC system, the 625 Group was dispatched to Turin to service the remaining lines, where it remained after the war, remaining in our hands.
FS Gruppo 623
FS Gr. 623
An evolution of the 625 Group designed with the scarcity of resources such as coal in mind, the 623 Group is equipped with the new Franco-Crosti boiler and various other improvements. More powerful than their predecessors and cheaper to operate, the higher axle load is not a problem on these relatively small engines, allowing them to operate in all but the least mantained lines. However, they remain less powerful than other locomotives, requiring multiple engines to haul the heaviest trains.

Braat Overvalwagen
Overvalwagen
Designed in 1940 and based on a Chevrolet COE (Cab Over Chassis) truck. In order to deflect or stop small arms fire, the sloped hull was 20 mm thick at the front glacis and 12 mm thick at the sides and rear. The main cab counted one driver armoured hinged panel and a side vision slit, while the commander position received a three-faced casemate housing an air-cooled cal.30 (7.62 mm) Browning machine gun or a liquid-cooled .303 (7.7 mm) Vickers and a rear hatch.

Carden Loyd Mk VI
V-CL Mk VI
The Royal Dutch Army had only a handful of either obsolete or worn-out armoured cars, twelve excellent DAF M39 six-wheeled armoured trucks, and five Carden Loyd Mark VI tankettes, named Lynx, Poema, Jaguar, Panter, and Luipaard.
DAF M39 Pantserwagen
DAF M39
For its time the DAF M39 was a modern design with an all-welded monocoque construction of the hull and extensive use of sloped armour. The turret, fitted with a relatively powerful 37 mm cannon, was produced in Sweden by Landsverk. The type was lightly armoured and relatively fast, with a good cross-country capability.
CTMS-1TB1
CTMS-1TB1
The CTMS-1TB1 project was started by Marmon-Herrington to produce a three-man light tank for the Dutch Army. It was armed with a 37 mm automatic cannon and coaxial M1919 machine gun. They originally meant to send 600 of them to the Dutch East Indies. However, the campaign ended too early for prototypes to be sent.
MTLS-1G14
MTLS-1G14
The MTLS-1G14 project was started at the same time as the CTMS-1TB1 to produce a four-man medium tank for the Dutch Army. It was armed with two 37 mm automatic cannons. It also was equipped with five M1919 machine guns, three of which were mounted on the hull, one mounted coaxially, and one mounted on the top of the turret. The armour was bolted and measured between 13-38 mm.

Braat AA

The Mannlicher Karabina vzor 1895/1930 (German: Infanterie Repetier-Gewehr M.95) was the service rifle of the Austro-Hungarian armed forces during the Weltkrieg. Kulometná pistole vzor 1934
Steyr-Solothurn vz. 34
While a German design by Louis Stange, the  MP 34 was mainly produced by Steyr and was adopted by the Austro-Hungarian Army. As common with early submachine guns, this design was heavy, expensive, but reliable, with a horizontal magazine using the potent 9x25mm Mauser cartridge.
Kulometná pistole vzor 38
Zbrojovka Brno vz. 38
Seeing the need for a submachine-gun using the standard pistol cartridge of the Army, the Monarchy would adopt the ZK 383, designed by brothers Josef and František Koucký at Zbrojovka Brno, as the MP 38. Using a horizontal magazine like the MP 34, the ZK 383 is known for having a light bipod, allowing it to be used as a substitute squad automatic weapon. Later models were heavily simplified for cheaper and faster production, along with a vertical foldable magazine like the Danuvia SMGs.
Kulometná pistole vzor 1943

While the Danuvia 39M proved successful, its folding magazine was not enough to compensate for its bulky design for vehicle crewmen. The 43M redesign with a folding metal stock and a new, more reliable foldable magazine design allowed it to be much more compact during transport or storage, without sacrificing firepower.

Mauser Gevär m/1896
Gevär m/96
Produced by the Mauser, the Gevär m/96 is a testament to Swedish engineering and military foresight. Chambered in the venerable 6.5x55mm cartridge, this bolt-action rifle has served Sweden with unmatched reliability. Its precision and durability make it a beloved tool among Swedish soldiers, ensuring its continued battlefield use. The m/96 remains a symbol of Swedish martial tradition, unaltered in its design and just as effective.
Mauser Gevär m/1932
Gevär m/32
Introduced in 1932, The Gevär m/32 continues to serve the Swedish armed forces with distinction. Its adoption, featuring slight modifications for improved ergonomics and accuracy, reflects Sweden's commitment to maintaining a formidable infantry force. Chambered in the efficient 6.5x55mm, the m/32 is a refined version of its predecessors, combining proven reliability with enhanced battlefield performance.
Automatgevär m/1939
AG m/39
The AG m/39, or AG Pelo, was initially dismissed due to its complexity and cost, but given time, the Swedish Arms Designer managed to make the long-recoil, semi-automatic rifle a reality. Chambered in 6.5x55mm, its adoption signifies Sweden's innovative approach to modern warfare, providing its soldiers with a powerful tool that balances complexity with lethal efficiency.
Automatgevär m/1942
AG m/42
Building on the AG m/39's foundation, the AG m/42 introduced numerous enhancements that redefined its battlefield role. Incorporating a stainless-steel gas tube, ergonomic modifications, and a new 10-round detachable magazine, alongside other improvements, solidifies its status as a superior weapon. Chambered in the standard 6.5x55mm, the AG m/42 is a testament to Swedish adaptability and technological advancement, offering soldiers a reliable, powerful, and refined weapon for the challenges ahead.

Bunduqiat Almsha Namudhaj 1898
Mauser B98
Mauser G98 was the main service rifle of the Ottoman Army during the Weltkrieg. The Ottoman M1903, chambered in 7.65mm, was the most common variant of Mauser in use. Pronounced 'Mavzer' by the Ottomans, this iconic rifle achieved great fame and became deeply ingrained in the Turkish subconscious.\n'One side of me withered from sorrows / the other from a Mavzer wound'. Freed from Ottoman control, the Palestinian army possess a large number of these rifles.
Albunduqiat Al'iimbiraturia Namudhaj 1355
Kırıkkale B55
Kırıkkale T55 was the name given to the Ottoman modification of Mauser Gewehr 98. Starting in 1933, the Ottoman Empire updated their old rifles to a common configuration known as the Model of 1936 and all in 8x57 Mauser cartridge. The standardisation of all Mausers in Ottoman inventory helped ease the logistical nightmare of having to supply 4 different types of rifle ammunition to all units.

SMB M1907 Chinese Mauser
SMB M1907
Originally produced as the Guangxu Type 33 during the Imperial rule as a close copy of the German Mauser Model 1904 with a special 6.8×57mm cartridge, but were later rechambered to the standard 7.92×57mm Mauser by 1915. While collectively inferior to newer rifles despite improvements, and often poorly maintained, the weapon is known to be rugged and reliable if unwieldy.\n\nThis variety is mainly produced at the Sichuan Machine Bureau, though equipment shortages and personal preference often see it used alongside non-standard weapons such as the Dadao.
Sichuan Type 27
Sichuan Type 27
Originally called the 'Type 27', this rifle was put into Qing service in 1935 through German assistance after the Restoration. The weapon is functionally a near copy of the German Mauser M1924, and a considerable improvement over the much older Type 88 in terms of weight and recoil.\n\nFirst produced at the Hanyang arsenal with German tools, manufacturing methods have already spread to Chengdu, though it may not fully replace its predecessors for some time.
$SHX_infantry_equipment_2$
$SHX_infantry_equipment_2_short$
Many Model 1921 Thompsons were imported into China during the 1920s, despite the USA being a leading adherent to an international embargo on the export of military weapons to that country. Copies were subsequently produced by at least three provincial arsenals. The Sichuan-made copies were stamped with the word 'Thampson' in misspelt recognition of the original designer and chambered to .45 ACP, resulting in ammunition shortage at one point due to its popularity.
Sichuan Xinhai Type 33
Sichuan Type 33
The Type 33 is a semi-automatic rifle based on the General Liu rifle from 1914. While appearing similar, the Type 33 is shorter, has the rear of the receiver covered, and the gas-trap system replaced by a simple gas port. The new rifle is also no longer able to switch to manual action and uses magazines from the Bohemian ZH-29 rifle and ZB-26 light machine gun.

Rifle, Calibre .30-06, Model 1903
M1903 Springfield
The Model 1903 was developed at Springfield Arsenal when, following the Spanish-American war, the United States deemed the Krag-Jørgensen rifle inadequate on account of its weak action; at its core, the 1903 was an attempt to combine beneficial features of both the Krag and captureds Spanish Mausers. Beginning just before the Weltkrieg, the rifle was gradually adopted along with the .30-06 cartridge, a process that would take several years.
Rifle, Calibre .30-06, Model 1903A1, Special Target
M1903A1 Springfield
The M1903A1 Springfield was adopted by the US Army in 1929 as the 'U.S. Rifle, Calibre .30-06, M1903A1'. It incorporated a pistol-grip, chequered buttplate, serrated trigger, and several smaller improvements into the original 1903 design.
Rifle, Calibre .30-06, Model 1937
M1937 Colt
With start of the Civil War, the new Army Department of the U.S. published a request for semi-automatic rifle designs. The Colt company submitted a .276 calibre rifle to the ensuing trials in 1938. The Colt M1937, the latest in a line of guns stemming from a design by J. E. Browning (half brother of John Moses Browning), is a gas-operated design using 108 parts. The M1937 was accepted in service in the end of 1938, after modification at the request of the Ordnance Department from .276 to .30-06 calibre.
Carbine, Calibre .30, Model 1942
M1942 Carbine
In 1940, the Ordnance Department put out a request for a new 'light rifle' or carbine, though the exact requirements for the weapon were not finalised until 1941. Colt did not submit a true carbine design, as it was otherwise pre-occupied, but with the death of J. E. Browning, they put contractor David Marshall Williams, who had begun work on a short-stroke gas piston design, on the project. Williams incorporated his short-stroke piston into an existing Colt prototype and shortened it in line with the requirements of the Ordnance department. The new rifle would eventually be accepted into service.
Submachine Gun, Calibre .45, Model 1928A1, Thompson

Anti-Tank Rifle, Calibre .50, Model 1942
M1942 Anti-Tank Rifle
The M1942 Anti-Tank Rifle was developed by David Marshall Williams at the request of the United States Army. Though the development process began soon after the war's outbreak, development took several years and was fraught with delays. The Williams Anti-Tank Rifle was finally adopted by the Army in 1942.
Recoilless Rifle, 2.2 inch, Model 1942
M1942 Recoilless Rifle
The M1942 Recoilless Rifle is a shoulder-fired anti-materiel weapon developed by the two engineers 'Kroger' and 'Musser' as part of a U.S. Army Infantry Section freelance project. The M1942 was developed in response to rapid improvements in armour which greatly diminished the effectiveness of anti-tank rifles small enough to be man-portable. The M1942 Recoilless Rifle has an effective range of 400 yards, a maximum range of nearly 5,000 yards, and is more accurate compared with the old M1942 anti-tank rifle. It quickly was nicknamed 'pocket artillery' by the soldiers who used it.

Infrared Sniperscope, Model 1943
M1943 Sniperscope
Developed specifically for the M1942A2 Auto-Carbine, which had special mountings on its receiver for various models of infra-red night-sighting devices, the M1943 Sniperscope is the first infrared sniperscope adopted for general use by the U.S. Army. While the M1943 has its flaws, like a poor range and an easily damaged Infrared emitter, the M1 still has tremendous value when used correctly.
Infrared Sniperscope, Model 1946
M1946 Sniperscope
In response to the poor reception of the M1943 Sniperscope, the Sniperscope M1946 was adopted. With almost twice the effective range of the M1943, a more robust infrared light source, and the T23 flash hider, the M1946 is a vast improvement over its predecessor, though some soldiers complain of the light source bleeding into the visible spectrum and thus giving away their position.

Ford Government, Large, Passenger, FWD
GLPFWD
The GLPFWD, also known as the 'Jeelp', is a Ford modification of the H-6 truck developed by the FWD company in 1930. Development of the vehicle itself started prior to the American Civil War and continued under the supervision of the rebel government. The H-6 was rebuilt on a 6x6 base and its capacity was increased to 2 1/2 tons by adapting lessons learned from the development of the ACKW truck by General Motors and the U.S. Army.
Tractor, High Speed, 13-ton, Model 1939A2, Carrier, Personnel
M1939A2 Tractor
The M1939 Tractor was developed on the chassis of the M3 'Lee' tank. Requested by the Army in 1939, as an artillery prime mover, it was redesigned as a personnel carrier in 1940. The M1939A2 can carry 10 soldiers and mounts two Browning guns. With impressive rough-terrain performance and solid reliability, the M1939A2 is considered a capable High-Speed Tractor.
Armoured Car, Carrier, Personnel, Model 1942
M1942 Carrier Car
In early 1942, the Army redesigned a Ford 6x4 truck for the personnel carrier role. The resulting vehicle, the M1942, is a low-silhouette, high-mobility, and lightly-armoured 6×6 vehicle capable of serving in a variety of roles. Possessing greater speed than its predecessor, the M1939 Tractor, the M1942 Car represents a large step forward in American carrier design.
Half-Track, Carrier, Personnel, Model 1943
M1943 Half-Track
The M1943 Half-Track was developed by Diamond T company on the basis of both the M1939 and a German design with a focus on parts interchangeability with commercial vehicle. Though lightly armoured, the resulting vehicle, the M1943, is particularly agile over rough terrain.
Ford Government, Rocket Launcher, FWD
GRLFWD
An FWD truck with a mounted M1941A6 rocket launcher, the GRLFWD is commonly known as the 'Girl'. While individual launchers are known to be a bit inaccurate, the volume of fire this design can output is impressive.
Ford Government, Rocket Launcher, FWD
GRLFWD
An FWD truck with a mounted M1941A6 rocket launcher, the GRLFWD is commonly known as the 'Girl'. While individual launchers are known to be a bit inaccurate, the volume of fire this design can output is impressive.
Landing Vehicle, Tracked, Model M1940A1
M1940A1 Landing Vehicle
The Landing Vehicle series of amphibious warfare vehicle were originally intended to serve solely as cargo carrier for ship to shore operations. They, of course, evolved into highly capable assault troop and fire support vehicles. Developed by Donald Roebling in 1935, the civilian rescue vehicle \
Landing Vehicle, Tracked, Model 1943
M1943 Landing Vehicle
The M1943 improved upon the M1940A1 with greatly increased carrying capacity, albeit at the expense of speed despite improvements to its engine. Unlike its predecessor, it also mounted either a heavy machine gun or a flame-thrower.
Scout Car, Model 1935
M1935 Scout Car
The M2 Scout Car is a lightly armoured, open topped, and machine gun armed four wheel drive vehicle developed for a reconnaissance role. A further development of the Scout Car concept, which was intended to replace cavalry in reconnaissance, the M2 Scout Car finished trials at the end of 1935, and amidst increasing tensions in the U.S. was accepted into Army service despite its flaws. In the new regime's service, the vehicle was known as the M1935.
Scout Car, Model 1939
M1939 Scout Car
The M1939 Scout Car is a development of the M1935 designed with experience gained during the Civil War in mind. The M1939 sports several small improves born of wartime experience, such as an armoured fender and front roller, and a more reliable engine. Although the Scout Car concept itself has received criticism for its focus on mobility over survivability, the M1939 was nonetheless accepted into service.
Armoured Car, Light, Model 1942
M1942 Armoured Car
The M1942 is a 6x6 armoured car produced by the Ford Motor Company. It was adopted as a reconnaissance anti-tank car, but its fast firing yet small 37-mm gun was found more suitable for an anti-infantry role The M1942's armour is thin, but is sufficient for its role.
Armoured Car, Model 1941A1
M1941A1 Armoured Car
The M1941 Armoured Car was developed by the Ford Motor Company. It was one of two designs submitted to meet a 1941 Ordnance Department requirement for a medium armoured car. Heavier than M1942 and designed around a 57-mm gun the car was adopted as the Army's first true anti-tank car.

Rifle No.1 Mk III
No.1 Mk III
With the collapse of the British Raj, the steady trickle of British rifles and ammunition into the country became a deluge and in the span of a year, Tibetan small arms advanced perhaps over fifty years. Further, the influx of German ammunition into Tibet following the German intervention in China led to Tibet converting its SMLE rifles to 7.65×53mm Mauser. The equipment shortages and personal preference often see it used alongside non-standard weapons such as the Dpa'dam.
Mauser Model 1898
Mauser 1898
In response to several commercially successful short rifles produced on the basis of the Mauser 1898 by competing arms manufacturers, the Mauser company developed its owned moderately shortened 1898 rifle. Two related patterns of this design were given the designation 'standard modell' by Mauser. Many small nations, including Tibet purchased these new guns in large quantities; the Tibetan variant is the older of the two and is chambered in 7.65×53mm Mauser.\nSoon after receiving the rifles, the Tibetan government converted several rifles to carbines, cannibalising older British rifles for material.

Rifle, Short, Magazine, Lee-Enfield Mk III
SMLE Mk III
The venerable Lee-Enfield (SMLE) rifle that served the Empire throughout the Great War continues to be the standard arm of the Dominions following the Empire's collapse. Quantities of the SMLE rifle can be found in arsenal throughout the many Dominions. With rifle production seriously disrupted with the loss of the arms factories of England, the Dominions have turned to the old reliable three-oh-three as their standard weapon of choice until suitable replacements are created or purchased.
SMLE Mk V
SMLE Mk V
After the fall of the Home Isles, the need to rearm what remained of the Empire became paramount. British engineers from the RSAF (Royal Small Arms Factory) began taking refuge in Ontario to work on an existing Lee-Enfield. The classic short magazine rifle's updated model displays a new and improved aperture system on the side instead of the middle, which features improved sighting radius, sighting accuracy, and sighting speed. However, due to the foraging and machining operations required to construct the rifle, the production of this new SMLE design is relatively expensive.
Owen Mk 1
Owen Machine Carbine
With the prospect of war coming, the Army has requested a submachine gun to be developed for close quarters and urban warfare, especially with the destructiveness that characterises the civil war in America. The Canadian Army officially adopted a weapon designed by young Australian private Evelyn Owen. The 
Long Branch Mk 1
SLR Mk 1
The Crown Corporation Small Arms Ltd in Long Branch responded to requests from the Canadian government for a self-loading rifle. The self-loading rifle is chambered in 8mm Mauser cartridges and features a tilting bolt action. While the gun suffers from reliability issues and excessive recoil, the rifle comes with a shoulder pad to compensate for the recoil. In addition, the rifle's light weight makes it ideal for mobility and urban combat. Many copies were sent to arm the Dominions of the Empire in preparation for the eventual homecoming.
Receivers, Tabby, Periscope Mk 1
Tabby Scope
The Tabby Scope is one of the Canadian government's most closesly guarded secrets; the process of development is even hidden from the fellow members of the Entente. A chance discovery by scientists in the ISAC, the scope is shaped in the form of a canteen but contains a monocular infrared scope along with a battery. Assigned to only the most elite of the elite, the scope allows the unprecedented advantage of having vision in the dark.
BSA Thompson M1926
The Canadian Army has formally adopted the iconic American submachine gun associated with crime and vice. The M1928A1 is the service variant of the classic M1921 Thompson Machine gun, and although production is expensive, the gun is well-liked among the troops in the field who praise its efficiency and reliability. While most variants rely on smaller 'box' magazines, some other variants feature large and bulky fifty-round drum magazines.
Lanchester Submachine Gun
With the outbreak of all out war in the United States and the looming clouds of war in Europe, the Canadian Army desperately needs arms for the homecoming. With little time to prepare and research, the Canadian Army has commissioned the 'Lanchester' submachine gun, a near perfect copy of the German MP-28.
Canadian Machine Carbine Mk 1
In further cooperation with the Small Arms Ltd at Long Branch, the Canadian military has officially adopted a new compliment and perhaps successor to the Owen. The Machine Carbine Mk 1 features a selective fire trigger with an innovative horizontal magazine to withstand dirt, dust, and sand. Pressure on the top of the trigger would fire the weapon in fully automatic, while pressure on the bottom would fire semi-automatic. While the new machine carbine features a lower rate of fire than the Owen, its reliability and ability to deal selective fire make it quite the potential successor. Many quantities found their way into the arsenal of the Dominions.
Grenade, Rifle, Anti-tank No. 68
Witnessing a demonstration of Henry Mohaupt's anti-tank rifle grenade in Switzerland, a Canadian commission, guessing that the weapon used the shaped charge principle, began work on their own design. The resulting high-explosive anti-tank (HEAT) rifle grenade is hoped to provide greater capabilities for the infantry to fight enemy armour using the cup launchers already in service.
Projector, Infantry, Anti Tank Mk I
With the need for a hand-held anti tank weapon for use on the frontlines, the Projector, Infantry, Anti Tank Mk I (PIAT) has been developed based on the design of the bombard mortar. With an effective range of 105 metres in direct fire mode, the device has been well liked due to its lack of backblast - however there has been concerns about its intense recoil.
PIAT
Vickers MG & Stokes mortar
The water cooled Vickers MG and the Stokes trench mortar were the standard support arms of the Canadian Army during the Weltkrieg. With the threat of war ever so near, the Canadian Army has recommissioned them back into service.
Lewis Mk III DEMS & SBML two-inch mortar
With its iconic 'pan' magazine, the Lewis has served the Tommy since the darkest days of the First Weltkrieg. With the threat of war ever so near, the MKIII variant has a pistol grip that allows it to be fired from the shoulder on any part of a ship's deck. The SBML while small, is incredibly portable and has greater firepower and range than most rifle grenades.
Vickers M Mk II & ML 3 inch mortar
The Mark II variant of the Vickers MG features a selective fire option and a pistol grip. It has been primarily adopted for the armoured vehicles. The ML 3 inch mortar is a considerable upgrade from the Stokes, as it is reliable and sturdy for close artillery support.
Vickers M Mk III & ML 4.2 inch Mortar
The third variant of the esteemed Vickers machine gun was designed for anti-aircraft usage and features a slightly increased rate of fire from its predecessors. Likewise, the 4.2 inch mortar is a heavier upgrade of previous Canadian mortar models and capable of dropping intense and effective support.

Ruskin Rhino
Rhino
With the success of the Rover under its belt, the Ruskin Motor Bodies company designed the Rhino in response to an Australasian government request for a substantially heavier armoured car built upon the CMP chassis. Though substantial changes were made to that CMP chassis, after much work the Rhino was born, and with substantial interchangeability of parts with other CMP-based designs to boot.
Ruskin Hippo
Hippo
To accommodate a substantially larger gun, the Rhino's coaxial machine had to be removed and its turret slightly enlarged. The 'Hippo' as this model has been designated, proved to be quite the headache for its design team, as these changes caused the already heavy vehicle to run into weight issues like its predecessors which had to be slowly worked out prior to the vehicle's adoption.

Maschinenpistole Modell 1934
Steyr-Solothurn M.34
While a German design by Louis Stange, the  MP 34 was mainly produced by Steyr and was adopted by the Austro-Hungarian Army. As common with early submachine guns, this design was heavy, expensive, but reliable, with a horizontal magazine using the potent 9x25mm Mauser cartridge.
Maschinenpistole Modell 38
Zbrojovka Brno M.38
Seeing the need for a submachine-gun using the standard pistol cartridge of the Army, the Monarchy would adopt the ZK 383, designed by brothers Josef and František Koucký at Zbrojovka Brno, as the MP 38. Using a horizontal magazine like the MP 34, the ZK 383 is known for having a light bipod, allowing it to be used as a substitute squad automatic weapon. Later models were heavily simplified for cheaper and faster production, along with a vertical foldable magazine like the Danuvia SMGs.
Maschinenpistole Modell 1943
Danuvia M.43
While the Danuvia 39M proved successful, its folding magazine was not enough to compensate for its bulky design for vehicle crewmen. The 43M redesign with a folding metal stock and a new, more reliable foldable magazine design allowed it to be much more compact during transport or storage, without sacrificing firepower.

Hvyntivka Mosina-Nagana zr.91
Hvyntivka zr.91
The 1891 Mosin-Nagant, chambered in 7.62x54R, has remained as the standard infantry rifle among Germany’s eastern allies following the collapse of the Russian Empire. With many of them facing chronic shortages of weaponry and unable to source new arms from Russia, local production of the rifle continued in Ukraine. While somewhat outdated compared to newer Mauser rifles, the Mosin-Nagant remains a cheap and reliable weapon for the Ukrainian army.
Hvyntivka Mosina-Nagana zr.91/27
Hvyntivka zr.91/27
The M/27 is a near-total reworking of the original Mosin-Nagant M1891, incorporating extensive improvements to enhance accuracy and durability. While retaining the receiver and magazine of its predecessor, the rifle features upgraded sights, bolt, a new bayonet, and a shorter yet heavy-profile 685mm barrel. Initially developed in Finland, the M/27 has since been produced in Ukraine with a licence, offering a more modern infantry rifle without abandoning existing stockpiles or production lines.
Pistolet-Kulemet zr. 1931
PK-31
The Suomi KP/31 is a Finnish submachine gun chambered in the widely used 9x19mm Parabellum cartridge. Entering service in 1931, its innovative design and high rate of fire quickly gained attention across Europe, leading to widespread licensing and local production, including in Ukraine. With a fire rate of up to 900 rounds per minute and a high-capacity drum magazine, it provides exceptional firepower in close combat. However, its considerable weight and demanding maintenance remain notable drawbacks.
Samozariadna Hvyntivka zr.1942
SH-42
The onset of the Second Weltkrieg saw the Russian army deploy a vast number of SVT-40 military rifles, granting them a significant edge in firepower. While the Ukrainian army could not effectively adopt the German SG-40 due to it being chambered in 7.92x57 Mauser, reverse-engineering captured SVTs allowed the Ukrainian arms industry to develop a new rifle chambered in 7.62X54R. While it is based primarily on the SG-40, the SH-42 is a cheaper design that incorporates the SVT's short-stroke piston gas system and detachable magazine.
Pistolet-Kulemet zr. 1928
PK-28
While the submachine gun concept was well-proven during the latter phase of the Weltkrieg, many nations see serious shortage of the weapon type. The MP-28, an improvement of the earlier MP-18 designed by Hugo Schmeisser, is a popular choice thanks to its relative ruggedness and affordability, along with Schmeisser's willingness to licence the design.
Karabin zr. 1939
Karabin zr. 1939
As the Weltkrieg drew near, there arose an urgent need for a cheap and reliable weapon for rear echelon troops. For the Oststaaten, the solution came in the form of a vastly shortened version of the Mosin-Nagant rifle. Drawing inspiration from the Model 1907 carbine and incorporating the design advancements of the Finnish M/27, a new carbine was developed. Featuring a shortened barrel and stock, the weapon measures just 1000 mm in total length, making it more compact and easier to handle for non-frontline personnel.

Fusil Mauser Modelo 1895
Modelo 1895
In response to an aggressive Argentinian armament programme, Chile adopted a modified Mauser 1893 (commonly known as the Spanish Mauser) chambered in 7x57mm Mauser, and contracted the German company DWM (Deutsche Waffen und Munitionsfabriken) for more than 100,000 rifles and carbines on the pattern. The Chilean Mauser 1895 has earned a reputation for reliability under even the harshest conditions, one which it maintains decades after its adoption. At the turn of the century, Uruguay purchased a substantial number of these rifles to replace its stopgap Dovitiis rifles.
Zbrojovka Brno Mauser Modelo 1932
Modelo 1932
The Zbrojovka Brno Version 1932 is a lightened and simplified version of Brno's earlier version 1924 carbine chambered in 7.65×53mm Mauser. Uruguay purchased a few thousand of these rifles in 1933 and quickly began small-scale domestic production.

Rifle, Calibre .30-06, Model 1903
M1903 Springfield
The Model 1903 was developed at Springfield Arsenal when, following the Spanish-American war, the United States deemed the Krag-Jørgensen rifle inadequate on account of its weak action; at its core, the 1903 was an attempt to combine beneficial features of both the Krag and captureds Spanish Mausers. Beginning just before the Weltkrieg, the rifle was gradually adopted along with the .30-06 cartridge, a process that would take several years.
Rifle, Calibre .30-06, Model 1903A1, Special Target
M1903A1 Springfield
The M1903A1 Springfield was adopted by the US Army in 1929 as the 'U.S. Rifle, Calibre .30-06, M1903A1'. It incorporated a pistol-grip, chequered buttplate, serrated trigger, and several smaller improvements into the original 1903 design.
Rifle, Calibre .30-06, Model 1
M1 Johnson
Designed by the eponymous Melvin Johnson, the rifle was adopted after Johnson successfully lobbied for the support of General MacArthur, who, despite the travails of past self-loading rifle development for the .30-06 cartridge, doggedly supported retaining the round. The M1 Johnson was fully adopted in early 1939 and designated as the 'U.S. Rifle, Calibre .30-06, M1'. It is a simple semi-automatic rifle with a few ingenious features like a two-piece stock and a unique 10-round rotary magazine fed by the same 5-round stripper clips already in use with the M1903 Rifle.
Automatic Carbine, Calibre .30, Model 2
M2 Auto-Carbine
The M2 Auto-Carbine is a development of the M1 Auto-Carbine, also known as the Johnson Carbine, which was developed by Melvin Johnson in the early 1940s. The M1 Auto-Carbine itself was based on the earlier Johnson Light Machine Gun, designed on the same principles as the even earlier Johnson Rifle. The Model 2 sports numerous small improvements over the M1 Auto-Carbine, such as a pistol grip and a new rear sight.
Submachine Gun, Calibre .45, Model 1928A1, Thompson
M1928A Thompson
Submachine Gun, Calibre .45, Model 2
M2 Grease Gun
Automatic Carbine, Calibre .30, Model 4

Anti-Mechanization Gun, Calibre .50, Model 2, Browning
M2 Anti-Mechanization Gun
The Second American Civil War necessitated the development of man-portable anti-vehicle weapons. As such, the U.S. Cavalry experimented with lightening and adapting the .50 calibre Browning M2 Heavy Machine Gun for man-portability. While heavier and bulkier compared with its European counterparts, the M2 Anti-Mechanization Gun was quickly adopted for service after satisfactory performance in Army trials.
Recoilless Rifle, 2.2 inch, Model 18
M18 Recoilless Rifle
The M18 Recoilless Rifle is a shoulder-fired anti-materiel weapon developed by the two engineers 'Kroger' and 'Musser' as part of a U.S. Army Infantry Section freelance project. The M18 was developed in response to rapid improvements in armour which greatly diminished the effectiveness of anti-tank rifles small enough to be man-portable. The M18 Recoilless Rifle has an effective range of 400 yards, a maximum range of nearly 5,000 yards, and is more accurate compared with the old M2. It quickly was nicknamed 'pocket artillery' by the soldiers who used it.

M5 Johnson MG & M2 mortar
Infrared Sniperscope, Model 1
M1 Sniperscope
Developed specifically for the M3 Auto-Carbine, which had special mountings on its receiver for various models of infra-red night-sighting devices, the M1 Sniperscope is the first infrared sniperscope adopted for general use by the U.S. Army. While the M1 has its flaws, like a poor range and an easily damaged Infrared emitter, the M1 still has tremendous value when used correctly.
Infrared Sniperscope, Model 3
M3 Sniperscope
In response to the poor reception of the M1 Sniperscope, the Sniperscope M3 was adopted. With almost twice the effective range of the M1, a more robust infrared light source, and the T23 flash hider, the M3 is a vast improvement over its predecessor, though some soldiers complain of the light source bleeding into the visible spectrum and thus giving away their position.
Harley-Davidson WLA
WLA
Class-B Standardized Military Truck
Class-B Truck
GMC 1936, Conventional cab, All-wheel drive, Dual rear axles
ACKW
The ACKW, officially the '1936 Conventional cab All-wheel drive Dual rear axles', commonly known as the 'Jimmy' or 'Deuce and a Half', is 2 and 1/2-ton load-rated 6x6 off-road capable tactical truck. Developed by the General Motors Company at the request of the U.S. Army Ordnance Corps in 1935, the ACKW comes in many variants, including open or closed cab and long or short wheel base models. The ACKW quickly became the U.S. army's standard truck and displayed great potential in logistical operations.
Carrier, Universal, Model 2
M2 Carrier
The M2 Carrier, also refferred to as the 'American Carrier', is based on the design of the Canadian Universal Carrier imported in the 1930s. Constructed by Willys-Overland Motor Company and modified to make use of largely Jeep automotive components, the M2 Carrier has better hill-climbing capabilities than Canadian carriers, but suffers from reliability issues.
Carrier, Universal, Model 4
M4 Carrier
The continuous development of carriers in the U.S. led to the appearance of the M4 Carrier. Built by Studebaker and developed with newest Canadian designs in mind, the M4 is an all-weather carrier designed as a basic chassis for many specialised roles, including a model for amphibious operations. With the ability to carry 6 soldiers, the M4 is in that regard more capable than its predecessor, but suffers from reliability issues without proper maintenance.
Carrier, Universal, Model 9
M9 Carrier
Designed around the chassis of M3 'Grant' tank, the M9 Carrier is a multi-role troop carrier with robust cross-country capabilities. Though the M9's top speed is a bit lower than the M4's, the M9 can carry more soldiers and is far more reliable. With enough space for auxiliary bits of infantry kit and thick armour, the M9 is a capable personal carrier.
GMC ACKW, M14
ACKW 'Xylophone'
The ACKW truck with the M14 rocket launcher - a modification of the M12 rocket launcher with the possibility of mounting on trucks - mounted ontop. It is commonly known as 'Xylophone' and is a model developed to fix the bad accuracy of the M12 by adding to it an additional rocket launcher. Whilst still being not very useful according to soldiers, the M14 showed itself effective during test trials and was accepted as the standard mobile rocket launcher of the U.S. army.
GMC ACKW, M14
ACKW 'Xylophone'
The ACKW truck with the M14 rocket launcher - a modification of the M12 rocket launcher with the possibility of mounting on trucks - mounted ontop. It is commonly known as 'Xylophone' and is a model developed to fix the bad accuracy of the M12 by adding to it an additional rocket launcher. Whilst still being not very useful according to soldiers, the M14 showed itself effective during test trials and was accepted as the standard mobile rocket launcher of the U.S. army.
Landing Vehicle, Tracked, Model 2
LVT-2
The LVT series of amphibious warfare vehicle were originally intended to serve solely as cargo carrier for ship to shore operations. They, of course, evolved into highly capable assault troop and fire support vehicles. Developed by Donald Roebling in 1935, the civilian rescue vehicle 
Landing Vehicle, Tracked, Model 4
LVT-4
The LVT-4 improved upon the LVT-2 with greatly increased carrying capacity, albeit at the expense of speed despite improvements to its engine. Unlike its predecessor, it also mounted either a heavy machine gun or a flame-thrower.
Scout Car, Model 2
M2 Scout Car
The M2 Scout Car is a lightly armoured, open topped, and machine gun armed four wheel drive vehicle developed for a reconnaissance role. A further development of the Scout Car concept, which was intended to replace cavalry in reconnaissance, the M2 Scout Car finished trials at the end of 1935, and amidst increasing tensions in the U.S. was accepted into Army service despite its flaws.
Scout Car, Model 3
M3 Scout Car
The M3 Scout Car is a development of the M2 designed with experience gained during the Civil War in mind. The M3 sports several small improves born of wartime experience, such as an armoured fender and front roller, and a more reliable engine. Although the Scout Car concept itself has received criticism for its focus on mobility over survivability, the M3 was nonetheless accepted into service.
Armoured Car, Model 5
M5 Armoured Car
After the end of Civil War, the U.S. Army Ordnance issued specifications for both medium and heavy armoured cars. In 1941, General Motors Company designed the T17 and T18 models, which were accepted as the M5 and M6 Armoured Cars. The M5 Armoured Car is an innovative design that incorporated some advanced features such as a two rear-facing 6-cylinder engines with automatic transmissions and steering and suspension components directly attached to the hull.
Armoured Car, Heavy, Model 6
M6 Armoured Car
After the end of Civil War, the U.S. Army Ordnance issued specifications for both medium and heavy armoured cars. In 1941, General Motors Company designed the T17 and T18 models, which were accepted as the M5 and M6 Armoured Cars. The M6 Armoured Car is similar to the M5 design, though substantially heavier. As such it was found to be less reliable than its lighter counterpart but more suitable for support roles.

Mle 1902 Indochinois

Mauser Modelo 1895 Rifle Corto
Mauser M1895
The Short Mauser Model 1895 is an upgraded Spanish Mauser in a configuration halfway between a full rifle and a carbine. The Costa-Rican variant is chambered in 7x57mm Mauser. Venezuela purchased a number of these rifles to replace its ageing Mauser 1871/84 rifles and also produced them domestically.

Rifle No.1 Mk III
No.1 Mk III
Rifle No.4 Mk I
No.4 Mk I
After the revolution and civil war it became apparent that the No.3 Enfield was not fit for urban combat. Trials for an entirely new rifle were finally held in 1932, but would largely fail to bear fruit, with new designs unable to match the old Enfield or receiving unfavourable troop evaluations. In light of this showing, Enfield replacement efforts were ultimately shelved. In 1935, however, a joint effort between The Revolutionary Small Arms factory in Enfield and Birmingham Small Arms was presented to the government. The new rifle was a development on the old Lee-Enfield with a shorter barrel, side mounted sling, and a simplified bolt system. While similar to its predecessors, the No.4 is stronger and easier to produce, though a bit heavier due to its barrel. An interesting fact about the No.4 is that it comes with an aperture sight that is set at increments of 100 yds (91m); calibrated for 200-1,300 yards (183-1189 metres).

Piachotnaja Vintouka uz.1891 Mosina
V-91
The 1891 Mosin-Nagant, chambered in 7.62x54R, has remained as the standard infantry rifle among Germany’s eastern allies following the collapse of the Russian Empire. With many of them facing chronic shortages of weaponry and unable to source new arms from Russia, local production of the rifle continued in Poland, Ukraine, and other Oststaaten with established arms industries. While somewhat outdated compared to newer Mauser rifles, the Mosin-Nagant remains a cheap and reliable weapon.
Piachotnaja Vintouka uz.1891/27 Mosina
V-91/27
The M/27 is a near-total reworking of the original Mosin-Nagant M1891, incorporating extensive improvements to enhance accuracy and durability. While retaining the receiver and magazine of its predecessor, the rifle features upgraded sights, bolt, a new bayonet, and a shorter yet heavy-profile 685mm barrel. Initially developed in Finland, the M/27 has since begun supplanting the older Mosin-Nagant across Eastern Europe, offering their troops a more modern infantry rifle without abandoning existing stockpiles or production lines.
Piachotny Pistaliet-Kuliamiot uz.1935 Bierhmana
PK-35
While the submachine gun concept was well-proven during the latter phase of the Weltkrieg, many nations see serious shortage of the weapon type as the Second Weltkrieg broke out. Unable to secure the German Army's standard MP-40, the Oststaaten often have to make due with what is commercially available through private firms. The MP-35, designed by Emil Bergmann and notable for its horizontal magazine on the right side, is a popular choice thanks to its relative ruggedness and affordability, along with Bergmann's willingness to license the design.
Samazaradnaja Vintouka uz. 1940 Tokareva
SV-40
At the onset of the Second Weltkrieg, the Russian army deployed vast numbers of the SVT-40 semi-automatic rifle, giving their forces a significant edge in firepower. With Belarus not having a self-loading rifle of its own, captured SVTs became a highly desirable asset. After successfully reverse-engineering the design, the Belarusian arms industry was able to produce a number of these rifles for the military.
Ruchny Minamiot uz.1943 Najmana
RMN-43
The RMN-43 was developed by Belarusian chemist Isaak Markovich Najman as Belarusian partisans required a portable weapon capable of launching explosives heavier than a rifle grenade, but lighter than a mortar. Najman's \
Procitankavaja Strelbu Braujera uz.1939
PTS-39
Reaktyunaja Procitankavaja Strelbu uz.1943
RPTS-43
The Raketenpanzerbuchse 54 shoulder-launched anti-tank rocket launchers, nicknamed 'Ofenrohr' ('stove pipe') and the more popular 'Panzerschreck' ('Tank's Fright'), are lightweight infantry weapons developed for the German military, inspired by the rumours about American rocket launchers. Under ideal conditions, the R.Pz.B. 54 can penetrate heavy tanks' armour with its 8,8-centimetre rockets, already used by the Raketenwerfer 43 rocket launchers. As a drawback, the R.Pz.B. 54 produces a lot of smoke upon firing. Many shipped over from Germany given Belarus' lack of anti tank weapons.

Fabrique Nationale Mauser Modèle 1889
FN M89
Fabrique Nationale Mauser Modèle 1935
FN M35
The Fabrique Nationale Model 1935 is a slightly shortned Model 1889 Mauser with a plethora of upgrades including a new bolt and locking system, a more reliable magazine, as well as improved ergonomics. The model made for the Belgian military is chambered in 7.65×53mm Mauser.
Pieper Bayard Modèle 1934
PB-34
Fabrique Nationale Modèle 1943
FN-43
Kunming Type 88
Kunming Type 88
Originally a product of late Guangxu era 'Self Strengthening' efforts, the Type 88 was designed as a close copy of the German Gewehr 88 with export modifications. While collectively inferior to newer rifles despite improvements, and often poorly maintained, the weapon is known to be rugged and reliable if unwieldy.\n\nThis variety is mainly produced at the Xining Arsenal in Qinghai, though equipment shortages and personal preference often see it used alongside non-standard weapons such as the Dadao.
Kunming Type 27
Kunming Type 27
Originally called the 'Type 27', this rifle was put into Qing service in 1935 through German assistance after the Restoration. The weapon is functionally a near copy of the German Mauser M1924, and a considerable improvement over the much older Type 88 in terms of weight and recoil.\n\nFirst produced at the Hanyang arsenal with German tools, manufacturing methods have already spread to Xining, though it may not fully replace its predecessors for some time.
Tsingtao MP18
Tsingtao MP18
Thanks to the flood of Weltkrieg surplus into the world market in the early 1920s, the MP18 saw action in China some time before a modified version began production in Tsingtao.\n\nWith changes to the magazine and stock, this particular product of Sino-German cooperation has been copied and sold throughout Northern and Southern China, though primarily to the Qing Government.
Hanyang Type 35
Hanyang Type 35
The Type 35 is a semi-automatic rifle based on the General Liu rifle from 1914. While appearing similar, the Type 35 is shorter, has the rear of the receiver covered, and the gas-trap system replaced by a simple gas port. The new rifle is also no longer able to switch to manual action and uses magazines from the Bohemian ZH-29 rifle and ZB-26 light machine gun.

Mauser Modelo 1902
Mauser M02
The Mauser Model 1902 is one of several Mauser rifles in service with the Mexican military, but is currently by far the most common. Chambered in 7x57mm, the Model 1902 is a highly modified Spanish Model 1893 Mauser integrating several parts and design elements from the later Mauser Model 1898. The Model 1902, which was purchased in large quantities from the German company DWM, is nearly identical to the domestically produced Model 1910.
Mondragón Modelo 1929
Mondragón M29
The revolutionary Mondragón Model 1908 was among the first semi-automatic rifles to see combat, even serving with the German Luftstreitkräfte during the Weltkrieg. While effective, the Mondragón has always suffered reliability issues and is expensive to produce. The Model 1929 is a modernised and easier to manufacture version of the original Mondragón.
Kunming Type 88
Kunming Type 88
Originally a product of late Guangxu era 'Self Strengthening' efforts, the Type 88 was designed as a close copy of the German Gewehr 88 with export modifications. While collectively inferior to newer rifles despite improvements, and often poorly maintained, the weapon is known to be rugged and reliable if unwieldy.\n\nThis variety is mainly produced at the Kunming Arsenal in Yunnan, though equipment shortages and personal preference often see it used alongside non-standard weapons such as the Dadao.
Kunming Type 27
Kunming Type 27
Originally called the 'Type 27', this rifle was put into Qing service in 1935 through German assistance after the Restoration. The weapon is functionally a near copy of the German Mauser M1924, and a considerable improvement over the much older Type 88 in terms of weight and recoil.\n\nFirst produced at the Hanyang arsenal with German tools, manufacturing methods have already spread to Kunming, though it may not fully replace its predecessors for some time.
Tsingtao MP18
Tsingtao MP18
Thanks to the flood of Weltkrieg surplus into the world market in the early 1920s, the MP18 saw action in China some time before a modified version began production in Tsingtao.\n\nWith changes to the magazine and stock, this particular product of Sino-German cooperation has been copied and sold throughout Northern and Southern China, though primarily to the Qing Government.
Kunming Xinhai Type 33
Kunming Type 33
The Type 33 is a semi-automatic rifle based on the General Liu rifle from 1914. While appearing similar, the Type 33 is shorter, has the rear of the receiver covered, and the gas-trap system replaced by a simple gas port. The new rifle is also no longer able to switch to manual action and uses magazines from the Bohemian ZH-29 rifle and ZB-26 light machine gun.

75mm Hanyang Xinhai Type 10 Field Gun
75mm Hanyang Type 10
As the most produced artillery during the Beiyang period, this artillery entered service in various armies by the Central Government and warlords across China.
Kunming Type Ziyuan
Ziyuan
After the outbreak of the American Civil War, many American engineers went into exile to escape the war. The Yunnan Machinery Bureau in Kunming seized the opportunity and recruited a group of engineers from the former US Stuart Motor Company. With the assistance of these engineers and the financial support of the Yunnan clique, the car named 'Ziyuan'(Resources) was officially put into production and entered military service.
